Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
intermediate
4 min
The Ash'ari Lineage and Abu Musa's Stature
Ibn Asakir praises the Ash'aris and highlights Abu Musa's stature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir establishes the honor of the Ash'aris through their early association with fiqh and the pivotal role of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari as a forefather of Imam Abu al-Hasan.

Core Idea
Lineage of knowledge: Abu Musa's fiqh honors the Ash'ari tradition.

Ibn Asakir begins by asserting the high status of the Ash'aris during the Prophet's time, describing them as renowned for jurisprudence and knowledge. He then singles out Abu Musa al-Ash'ari as the most prominent figure, noting that he is the grandfather of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. This lineage serves to elevate the Ash'ari school by connecting it directly to a Companion known for his learning.

Guided Path
1
Read the praise of the Ash'aris
Carefully read the first sentence where Ibn Asakir describes the Ash'aris as being known for fiqh in the Prophet's time. Notice how this establishes their early credentials.
2
Identify the specific mention of Abu Musa
Find the clause where Abu Musa is called the most famous in fiqh and knowledge, and note his relation to Imam Abu al-Hasan. Ask yourself why this connection matters.
3
Reflect on the significance of lineage
Consider how linking the Ash'ari school to a Companion like Abu Musa gives it scholarly legitimacy. This is a common theme in early Sunni biographical literature.
4
Appreciate the concluding statement
Read the final sentence of the passage: 'So virtue came to him from that direction, and he who resembles his father is not wronged.' This reinforces the idea of inherited excellence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالأشعريون بالفقه في زمن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم موصوفون، وبالعلم عند الاعلام من الصحابة رضى الله عنهم ،معروفون وأشهرهم بالفقه والعلم في ذلك الزمن أبو موسى الأشعرى، جد الإمام أبي الحسن وكفاه بذلك عند العلماء شرفاً وفضلاً، وما أسعد من كان أبو موسى له سلفاً وأصلاً، فالفضل ذلك الوجه أتاه وما ظلم من أشبه أباه . من فهذا بعض ما حضرنى من فضل الأشعريين على العموم فأما ما ورد في فضل أبي موسى وولده خصوصا من الفضل المعلوم فأخبرنا الشيوخ أبو يعقوب يوسف بن أيوب الهمذاني بمرور وأبو بكر محمد بن الحسين الفرضى وأبو منصور عبد الرحمن بن محمد القزاز وأبو محمد بن يحيى بن على بن محمد مدير الحكم قالوا أنا عبد الصمد بن علی بن محمد العباس أنا على ابن عمر بن أحمد الدار قطنی، نا أحمد بن علی بن العلاء نا يوسف بن موسى وأحمد بن محمد بن أبى السفر قالوا نا أبو أسامة عن بريد عن أبي بردة عن أبي موسى رضى الله عنه قال خرجنا مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فى غزاة ونحن ستة نفر بيننا بعير نتعقبه وقال ابن أبي السفر نتعقبه قال فنقبت أقدامنا قال أبو موسى ونقبت قدمای و تشققت أظنمارى فكنا نلف على أرجلنا الخرق قال أبو بردة فحدث أبو موسى بهذا الحديث ثم كره ذلك فقال ماكنت أصنع أن أذكر هذا الحديث قال كأنه كره أن يفشى شيئاً من عمله وقال يوسف كأنه كره أن يكون شيء من عمله أفشاه قال وزاد غير بريد والله يجزى به هذا لفظ يوسف يعني ابن موسی رواه البخارى ومسلم عن أبى بكير عن أسامة. أخبرنا أبو القسم بن الحصين أنا أبو على بن المذهب أنا أبو بكر بن مالك نا عبد الله بن أحمد حدثني أبى نا روح نا سعيد عن قتادة قال حدث أبو بردة عن عبد الله بن قيس عن أبيه قال قال أبى لو شهدتنا ونحن مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذ أصابتنا السماء حسبت أن ريحنا ريح الضأن إنما لباسنا الصوف
The Ash‘arīs are described with jurisprudence (fiqh) in the time of the Messenger of Allāh (peace be upon him), and they are known for knowledge among the notables of the Companions (may Allāh be pleased with them). The most famous of them in jurisprudence and knowledge in that time was Abū Mūsā al-Ash‘arī, the grandfather of Imām Abū al-Ḥasan, and that suffices him among scholars as honor and virtue. How fortunate is he whose forefather and origin was Abū Mūsā! So virtue came to him from that direction, and he who resembles his father is not wronged. This is some of what came to mind concerning the virtue of the Ash‘arīs in general. As for what has been reported concerning the virtue of Abū Mūsā and his sons specifically from known virtue, our shaykhs informed us: Abū Ya‘qūb Yūsuf ibn Ayyūb al-Hamadhānī in Marw, and Abū Bakr Muḥammad ibn al-Ḥusayn al-Faraḍī, and Abū Manṣūr ‘Abd al-Raḥmān ibn Muḥammad al-Qazzāz, and Abū Muḥammad ibn Yaḥyā ibn ‘Alī ibn Muḥammad Mudīr al-Ḥakam – they said: ‘Abd al-Ṣamad ibn ‘Alī ibn Muḥammad al-‘Abbās told us: ‘Alī ibn ‘Umar ibn Aḥmad al-Dāraquṭnī told us: Aḥmad ibn ‘Alī ibn al-‘Alā’ told us: Yūsuf ibn Mūsā and Aḥmad ibn Muḥammad ibn Abī al-Safar told us – they said: Abū Usāmah told us from Burayd from Abī Burda from Abū Mūsā (may Allāh be pleased with him) – he said: We went out with the Messenger of Allāh (peace be upon him) on an expedition while we were six persons, having one camel between us which we rode alternately – and Ibn Abī al-Safar said: we rode it alternately – he said: Then our feet became sore. Abū Mūsā said: My feet became sore and my nails cracked, so we used to wrap rags on our feet. Abū Burda said: Abū Mūsā narrated this hadith, then disliked that, and said: What am I doing mentioning this hadith? He said: It was as if he disliked spreading anything of his deeds. Yūsuf said: It was as if he disliked that any of his deeds be spread. He said: And besides Burayd added: 'By Allāh, He will reward for this.' This is the wording of Yūsuf, meaning Ibn Mūsā. Al-Bukhārī and Muslim narrated it from Abī Bakr from Usāmah. We were informed by Abū al-Qāsim ibn al-Ḥuṣayn: Abū ‘Alī ibn al-Madhhab told us: Abū Bakr ibn Mālik told us: ‘Abd Allāh ibn Aḥmad told me – my father told us: Rawḥ told us: Sa‘īd from Qatādah said: Abū Burda narrated from ‘Abd Allāh ibn Qays from his father – he said: My father said: If only you had seen us with the Messenger of Allāh (peace be upon him) when the sky [rain] hit us – I thought our smell was the smell of sheep, for our clothing was wool.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a combination of authorial praise and two hadith narrations about the virtue of the Ash‘arīs and especially Abū Mūsā al-Ash‘arī. Ibn ‘Asākir first states that the Ash‘arīs were described with fiqh (jurisprudence) during the Prophet’s time and were known for knowledge among the Companions. He singles out Abū Mūsā al-Ash‘arī as the most famous in fiqh and knowledge, noting that he is the grandfather of Imām Abū al-Ḥasan al-Ash‘arī. This lineage gives the Ash‘arī school great honor. The author then presents a hadith with multiple chains about Abū Mūsā’s hardship on an expedition: six companions sharing one camel, their feet getting sore, nails cracking, and wrapping rags. Abū Mūsā initially narrated this but then disliked doing so, showing his humility and desire to hide his good deeds. The hadith is attributed to Bukhārī and Muslim. Next, another hadith describes the companions’ rough woolen clothing, which made them smell like sheep. This demonstrates the asceticism and hard life of the early Muslims, including Abū Mūsā, further emphasizing his virtue.

Key Terms
الأشعريون
أبو موسى الأشعري
الفقه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Ash'ari school has no connection to the Companions and is a later theological innovation.
Correction: Ibn Asakir shows that the Ash'aris were known for fiqh in the Prophet's time, and that Abu Musa, a Companion, is the grandfather of Imam Abu al-Hasan, linking the school to early Islamic scholarship.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Asakir, who was the most famous Ash'ari in fiqh and knowledge during the Prophet's time?
A) Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari
B) Abu Musa al-Ash'ari
C) Abu Bakr al-Faradi
D) Abu Ya'qub al-Hamadhani

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari school traces its scholarly lineage back to the Companion Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, who was renowned for fiqh in the Prophet's era.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to follow the Ash'ari tradition, which traces its scholarly lineage back to Abu Musa and the Companions. But does your daily life reflect that noble ancestry? Are you actively seeking knowledge and practicing fiqh, or are you content with a distant lineage without resemblance?
?
The proverb says: 'he who resembles his father is not wronged.' Who are your spiritual fathers—the scholars and righteous predecessors you claim to follow? Do you truly resemble them in character, worship, and commitment to truth? If not, what concrete step can you take today to start resembling them?
?
Ibn Asakir highlights that the Ash'aris were already described with fiqh in the Prophet's own time. You belong to a tradition that was present at the very source of Islam. Does that honor fill you with gratitude and responsibility, or have you taken it for granted? What will you do to honor that heritage this week?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
intermediate
5 min
The Humility of Abu Musa: Hiding Good Deeds
Ibn Asakir narrates hadiths showing Abu Musa's hardship and humility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith about Abu Musa's hardship during an expedition and the lesson it teaches about concealing one's good deeds and maintaining humility.

Core Idea
True piety hides one's sacrifices.

In this lesson, we examine a hadith narrated by Abu Musa himself about an expedition where he and five companions shared one camel, suffered sore feet, and cracked nails. After narrating this, Abu Musa expressed regret, disliking that his deeds be publicized. This story, along with a second hadith about their rough wool clothing, powerfully illustrates the early Muslims' asceticism and their desire to hide their good works.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic and translation of the first hadith. Note the details: six people, one camel ridden alternately, sore feet, cracked nails, wrapping rags.
2
Observe Abu Musa's reaction
After narrating, Abu Musa disliked what he did. The narrators explain he did not want to spread his deeds. This is the key lesson.
3
Reflect on the second hadith
The second hadith describes their wool clothing smelling like sheep. This reinforces the theme of hardship and simplicity.
4
Connect to the value of ikhlas
Both narrations show that the early Muslims prioritized sincerity (ikhlas) by avoiding fame for their sacrifices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The most famous of them in jurisprudence and knowledge in that time was Abū Mūsā al-Ash‘arī, the grandfather of Imām Abū al-Ḥasan, and that suffices him among scholars as honor and virtue. Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Abu Musa was primarily a military leader with little spiritual depth.
Correction: This hadith shows his deep humility and desire to conceal his sacrifices, emphasizing his spiritual virtue and fear of ostentation.

Checkpoint
Why did Abu Musa dislike narrating the hadith about his sore feet?
A) He felt the hadith was weak
B) He did not want to spread his good deeds
C) He forgot the details
D) He was ordered by the Prophet not to narrate

Key Takeaway
Abu Musa's regret over narrating his hardship teaches us the importance of hiding our good deeds to maintain sincerity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of the last time you mentioned a good deed you did. Was there a part of you that wanted others to know? How can you train your heart to seek only Allah's recognition, as Abu Musa did when he regretted speaking of his hardship?
?
Abu Musa wrapped rags on his feet and wore wool that smelled like sheep. If someone saw your lifestyle today, would they see a person content with the dunya's hardships for the sake of the Prophet's company? What needs to change in your life to genuinely embrace that spirit?
?
After reading that Abu Musa disliked 'spreading anything of his deeds', ask yourself: have I ever felt uncomfortable when someone praised my generosity or piety? If not, what is blocking that discomfort? Write one practical step you will take this week to hide a good deed from others.

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
5 min
The Ash'ari Legacy: Praise of Imam al-Ash'ari's Lineage
Ibn Asakir praises the Ash'ari school and highlights Abu Musa's virtue.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir establishes the honor of the Ash'ari school by linking it to the early generation of Companions, especially Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, and why this lineage is considered a mark of virtue in Sunni scholarship.

Core Idea
The Ash'ari school traces its scholarly and moral roots back to the Prophet's Companions.

In this passage, Ibn Asakir offers a brief but powerful tribute to the Ash'ari school. He does not discuss theological arguments; instead, he anchors the school's prestige in the early Islamic period, highlighting that the Ash'aris were known for fiqh and knowledge even in the time of the Companions. He then singles out Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, the grandfather of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, as the exemplar of this tradition. This lesson explores how this historical connection serves as a source of honor and legitimacy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the literal English translation. Notice the concise yet powerful style of Ibn Asakir.
The passage is a single flowing paragraph.
2
Understand the claim about the Ash'aris
Ibn Asakir states that the Ash'aris were 'described by fiqh' during the Prophet's time and known for knowledge among the Companions. This is a strong assertion linking them to the earliest generation.
Fiqh here means deep understanding of religious law.
3
Identify Abu Musa al-Ash'ari
Abu Musa is singled out as the most famous in fiqh and knowledge. Note that he is the grandfather of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, the founder of the Ash'ari school.
Abu Musa was a prominent Companion and a governor during the caliphates of Umar and Uthman.
4
Reflect on the significance of lineage
Ibn Asakir describes this ancestry as a 'suffice as honor and virtue' and says 'how fortunate is he whose predecessor was Abu Musa'. This establishes a spiritual and intellectual lineage.
The phrase 'who resembles his father has not been wronged' is a proverb implying that Imam al-Ash'ari inherited virtue.
5
Address potential misunderstanding
This passage is not about doctrinal theology but about historical reputation. Recognize that Ibn Asakir is using genealogy and early Islamic credentials to praise the school.
This is a common literary device in biographical works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالأشعريون بالفقه في زمن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم موصوفون، وبالعلم عند الاعلام من الصحابة رضى الله عنهم ،معروفون وأشهرهم بالفقه والعلم في ذلك الزمن أبو موسى الأشعرى، جد الإمام أبي الحسن وكفاه بذلك عند العلماء شرفاً وفضلاً، وما أسعد من كان أبو موسى له سلفاً وأصلاً، فالفضل ذلك الوجه أتاه وما ظلم من أشبه أباه .
The Ash'aris are described by fiqh in the time of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and are known for knowledge among the notables of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them. And the most famous of them in fiqh and knowledge in that time was Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, the grandfather of Imam Abu al-Hasan. And that suffices as honor and virtue in the eyes of the scholars. And how fortunate is he whose predecessor and origin was Abu Musa. So virtue came to him from that direction, and he who resembles his father has not been wronged.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a biographical encomium praising the Ash'ari school and specifically highlighting Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, the grandfather of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. Ibn Asakir begins by stating that the Ash'aris were described by fiqh (deep understanding of religious law) during the Prophet's time, and were known for knowledge among the notable Companions. He then singles out Abu Musa as the most famous of them in fiqh and knowledge in that era. Abu Musa's status as the grandfather of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari is mentioned as a source of honor and virtue. The passage ends with a proverbial expression indicating that whoever resembles his father (i.e., inherits his virtues) has not been wronged, implying that Abu al-Hasan inherited the virtue of his grandfather.

Key Terms
أشعريون
أبو موسى الأشعري
أبو الحسن الأشعري
فقه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think this passage contains theological arguments for Ash'arism or that it is a doctrinal statement.
Correction: Ibn Asakir is not making a theological case here; he is establishing the historical and familial honor of the Ash'ari school, using biography and genealogy.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Asakir, why is Abu Musa al-Ash'ari notable?
A) He was a famous theologian.
B) He was the most famous of the Ash'aris in fiqh and knowledge during the Prophet's time.
C) He was the founder of the Ash'ari school.
D) He was a Companion known for his poetry.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir elevates the Ash'ari school by tying it to the Companions, especially Abu Musa, showing that its origin lies in early Islamic piety and knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In this lesson, Ibn Asakir draws honor from his connection to a righteous ancestor. Who in your own life—whether a scholar, parent, or spiritual guide—has given you a legacy of faith? What have you done to honor that connection, and what more could you do today?
?
The passage ends with 'he who resembles his father has not been wronged.' If you look at your own character, do you see a resemblance to those who taught you Islam? What specific quality would you be ashamed to admit you lack, and what step will you take this week to acquire it?
?
Ibn Asakir takes pride in the Ash'ari lineage tracing back to a Companion. But pride in lineage is only valuable if it motivates action. Are you content to merely boast about the scholars you follow, or are you actively seeking to embody their knowledge and piety? What is one concrete practice from the way of the Ash'aris that you will commit to starting tomorrow?

Abu Musa's Blistered Feet and the Virtue of Modesty
Narration of Abu Musa describing hardship and his regret for publicizing it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Companion Abu Musa's reluctance to narrate his suffering teaches the Islamic virtue of modesty and avoiding self-publicity.

Core Idea
True piety hides one's good deeds; Abu Musa regretted even mentioning his hardship.

This lesson presents a hadith narrated by Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, in which he describes the physical hardships he and his fellow Companions endured during an expedition with the Prophet (PBUH). More importantly, it captures Abu Musa's moment of regret after narrating the incident, revealing his deep sense of modesty and his desire not to make his own sacrifices known. Through this story, we learn a profound lesson about humility and sincerity.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its chain
Read the Arabic text and translation carefully. Notice the careful chain of transmission (isnad) and the details of the hardship.
The chain includes several narrators, showing the care in preserving the report.
2
Identify the key teaching: Abu Musa's regret
Focus on the part where Abu Musa expresses dislike for narrating the hadith. Why does he feel this way?
3
Reflect on the virtue of modesty
Consider how this hadith teaches us to avoid seeking fame for our good deeds. What does it reveal about the character of the Companions?
This connects to the broader Islamic concept of ikhlas (sincerity).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخبرنا الشيوخ أبو يعقوب يوسف بن أيوب الهمذاني بمرور وأبو بكر محمد بن الحسين الفرضى وأبو منصور عبد الرحمن بن محمد القزاز وأبو محمد بن يحيى بن على بن محمد مدير الحكم قالوا أنا عبد الصمد بن علی بن محمد العباس أنا على ابن عمر بن أحمد الدار قطنی، نا أحمد بن علی بن العلاء نا يوسف بن موسى وأحمد بن محمد بن أبى السفر قالوا نا أبو أسامة عن بريد عن أبي بردة عن أبي موسى رضى الله عنه قال خرجنا مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فى غزاة ونحن ستة نفر بيننا بعير نتعقبه وقال ابن أبي السفر نتعقبه قال فنقبت أقدامنا قال أبو موسى ونقبت قدمای و تشققت أظنمارى فكنا نلف على أرجلنا الخرق قال أبو بردة فحدث أبو موسى بهذا الحديث ثم كره ذلك فقال ماكنت أصنع أن أذكر هذا الحديث قال كأنه كره أن يفشى شيئاً من عمله وقال يوسف كأنه كره أن يكون شيء من عمله أفشاه قال وزاد غير بريد والله يجزى به هذا لفظ يوسف يعني ابن موسی رواه البخارى ومسلم عن أبى بكير عن أسامة.
The scholars Abu Ya'qub Yusuf ibn Ayyub al-Hamadhani, and Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Faradi, and Abu Mansur 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Muhammad al-Qazzaz, and Abu Muhammad ibn Yahya ibn 'Ali ibn Muhammad Mudir al-Hukm informed us, saying: 'Abd al-Samad ibn 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-'Abbas informed us, 'Ali ibn 'Umar ibn Ahmad al-Daraqutni informed us, Ahmad ibn 'Ali ibn al-'Ala' informed us, Yusuf ibn Musa and Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Abi al-Safar said: Abu Usama narrated to us from Burayd from Abu Burda from Abu Musa, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: We set out with the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, on an expedition, and we were six persons sharing one camel which we rode alternately.' Ibn Abi al-Safar said, 'We rode it alternately.' He said, 'Then our feet became blistered.' Abu Musa said, 'My feet became blistered and my nails cracked, so we used to wrap rags around our feet.' Abu Burda said: Abu Musa narrated this hadith, then he disliked it and said, 'I should not have mentioned this hadith.' He [Abu Burda] said: It was as if he disliked to publicize any of his actions. Yusuf said: It was as if he disliked that any of his actions be publicized. He said, 'And other than Burayd added: 'And Allah will reward for it.' This is the wording of Yusuf, meaning Ibn Musa. It was narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim from Abu Bukayr from Usamah.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a hadith narration about the hardships endured by the Companions during a military expedition with the Prophet (PBUH). The chain of transmission is given at length. The content: Abu Musa describes that they were six people sharing one camel, and their feet became blistered. Specifically, his feet blistered and his nails cracked, so they wrapped rags around their feet. After narrating this, Abu Musa seemed to regret it, as he disliked publicizing his deeds. The additional narration from Yusuf clarifies that he disliked any of his actions being made public. The hadith is attributed to al-Bukhari and Muslim. The lesson here is the virtue of modesty and not seeking fame for one's good deeds.

نقبت أقدامنا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Abu Musa regretted narrating the hadith because he thought it was unimportant or complained about hardship.
Correction: The text clearly states he disliked publicizing his actions; his regret was due to modesty, not any issue with the story's truthfulness.

Checkpoint
Why did Abu Musa feel reluctant about narrating the hadith of his blistered feet?
A) He thought the story was unimportant.
B) He disliked making his own deeds public.
C) He was embarrassed about complaining.
D) He forgot the details.

Key Takeaway
Abu Musa's regret shows that true believers avoid publicizing their good deeds, seeking only Allah's reward.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The Prophet's companions hid their sacrifices. Is there an area in your life where you seek validation from people instead of Allah? What concrete step can you take today to shift that to sincerity?

The Companions' Wool Clothing in Rain
Short narration about the Companions' wool clothing in rain.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of the Companions' simple clothing and how it reflects their devotion and hardship alongside the Prophet.

Core Idea
The Companions' wool clothing in rain shows their simple, devoted lifestyle with the Prophet.

This lesson presents a brief but powerful narration from the Companion Abu Musa al-Ash'ari's father, describing the humble condition of the Companions during the Prophet's time. The image of them smelling like sheep due to their wool garments underscores their asceticism and closeness to the Prophet. Let's examine the chain and the lesson it teaches.

Guided Path
1
Read the narration and its chain
Read the Arabic text and translation, noting the chain of transmission. See how the hadith is traced back to a Companion.
The chain is strong, showing reliable transmission.
2
Reflect on the description
Consider what the narrator says: their smell was like sheep because their clothing was only wool. What does this tell you about their lifestyle?
Think about the simplicity and hardship.
3
Understand the lesson
Ask: Why is this narrated? It is not a complaint but a testament to their simple faith and dedication.
This narration highlights their devotion, not poverty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخبرنا أبو القسم بن الحصين أنا أبو على بن المذهب أنا أبو بكر بن مالك نا عبد الله بن أحمد حدثني أبى نا روح نا سعيد عن قتادة قال حدث أبو بردة عن عبد الله بن قيس عن أبيه قال قال أبى لو شهدتنا ونحن مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذ أصابتنا السماء حسبت أن ريحنا ريح الضأن إنما لباسنا الصوف
Abu al-Qasim ibn al-Husayn informed us, Abu 'Ali ibn al-Madhhab informed us, Abu Bakr ibn Malik informed us, 'Abdullah ibn Ahmad narrated to us, my father narrated to me, Rawh narrated to us, Sa'id narrated to us from Qatada who said: Abu Burda narrated from 'Abdullah ibn Qays from his father who said: My father said, 'If you had seen us when we were with the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and the rain fell upon us, you would have thought that our smell was the smell of sheep; our clothing was only wool.'
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a short narration about the simple and rough lifestyle of the Companions during the time of the Prophet (PBUH). The chain is given. The content: Abu Musa's father (Abdullah ibn Qays) says that if people saw them with the Prophet when rain fell, they would think their smell was like sheep because their clothing was only wool. This highlights the asceticism and hardship the Companions endured, and their closeness to the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
The Companions' simple wool clothing in rain reflects their ascetic devotion alongside the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Companions wore only wool, not because they couldn't afford better, but because they chose simplicity to be with the Prophet. What does your choice of clothing, lifestyle, or luxury reveal about your attachment to this world? Are you willing to give up a comfort for the sake of drawing nearer to Allah, like they did?
?
Imagine your own smell being noticeable because of your devotion. Would you be embarrassed or honoured like the Companions? This hadith shows they didn't mind. What does that say about your own fears of how others see you? Commit to one act today that prioritises your relationship with Allah over public perception.

The Martyrdom of Abu 'Amir and the Prophet's Prayer
Narration of Abu 'Amir's wound and the Prophet's prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the story of Abu 'Amir's martyrdom and the Prophet's prayer for him and Abu Musa, highlighting the Prophet's compassion and the virtue of seeking forgiveness.

Core Idea
The Prophet's prayer for his companions shows his deep mercy and care for their salvation.

This passage narrates a crucial event after the Battle of Hunayn. The Prophet sends Abu 'Amir to pursue the enemy, and during the mission he is fatally wounded. The hadith shows the Prophet's immediate response of prayer and forgiveness for his fallen companion, as well as his care for Abu Musa who conveyed the request. Through this story, we see the Prophet's compassion and the honour accorded to these companions.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith narrative
Read the Arabic passage from the chain through the story of Abu 'Amir's wound and death, including the Prophet's prayer for both Abu 'Amir and Abu Musa.
Notice the detail of the Prophet's simple bed as a sign of his humility.
2
Identify key events
Track the sequence: the battle, Abu 'Amir being shot, Abu Musa pursuing the shooter, removing the arrow, the request for forgiveness, and the Prophet's double prayer.
The water gushing from the wound indicates the severity.
3
Reflect on the Prophet's prayer
Consider why the Prophet specifically prayed for Abu 'Amir to be raised above many people, and for Abu Musa's forgiveness and noble entrance.
This shows the Prophet's concern for their afterlife status.
4
Connect to the lesson objective
Relate the narrative to the learning objective: the Prophet's mercy and the importance of seeking forgiveness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأخبرنا الشيخ أبو عبد الله محمد ابن الفضل الفراوي الفقيه أنا أبو بكر أحمد بن منصور بن خلف المغربي أنا أبوبكر محمد بن عبدالله بن معتمد الجوزقى أنا أبوالعباس الدغولی نا محمد بن سليمان القيراطی نا أبو أسامة نا بريد بن عبد الله قال الجوزقى وأنا أبو جعفر محمد بن الحسن بن اسحق الأصبهاني نا أبو البخترى عبد الله بن محمد بن شاكر نا أبو أسامة نا بريد بن عبد الله بن أبي بردة عن أبي بردة عن أبي موسى رضى الله عنه قال لما فرغ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من حنين بعث أبا عامر على الجيش إلى أوطاس فلقى دريد بن الصمة فقتل الله دريداً وهزم أصحابه قال أبو موسى وبعثنى مع أبي عامر قال فرمى أبو عامر في ركبته رماه رجل من بنی چشم بسهم فأثبته في ركبته فانتهيت إليه فقلت ياعم من رماك فأشار أبو عامر إلى أبي موسى فقال إن ذلك قاتلى يريد ذاك الذي رماني فأتيته وجعلت أقول له ألا تستحيى الست عربياً فكف فالتقيت أنا وهو ضربتين فضربته بالسيف فقتلته ثم رجعت إلى أبي عامر فقلت له قد قتل صاحبك قال فانزع هذا السهم فنزعته فنزا منه الماء فقال يا أخى انطلق إلى رسول الله فأقرئه منى السلام وقل له أنه يقول لك استغفر لي قال واستخلفنى أبو عامر على الناس قال فمكث يسيراً ثم أنه مات فلما رجعت إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم دخلت عليه وهو في بيت على سرير مرمل وعليه فراش قد أثر رمال السرير بظهر رسول الله وجنبيه فأخبرته بخبرنا وخبر أبي عامر فقلت يقول لك استغفر لى فدعا رسول الله له بماء فتوضا ثم رفع يديه وقال ( اللهم اغفر لعبيد أبي عامر حتى رأيت بياض ابطيه، ثم قال اللهم اجعله يوم القيامة فوق كثير ممن خلقت أو من الناس فقلت ولى يارسول الله، فاستغفر لي فقال اللهم اغفر لعبد الله بن قيس ذنبه وادخله يوم القيامة مدخلاً كريماً ) قال أبو بردة احداهما لأبي عامر والأخرى لأبي موسی، رواه البخاري ومسلم عن أبى كريب عن أبي أسامة، وفي هذا الحديث بشارة لأبي الحسن رحمه الله بدخوله في استغفار الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم إذ فيه وفى غيره إشارة إلى ذلك لا تخفى على ذوى العقول.
And the Shaykh Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Farawi al-Faqih informed us, Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Mansur ibn Khalaf al-Maghribi informed us, Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn Mu'tamad al-Jawzaqi informed us, Abu al-Abbas al-Daghuli informed us, Muhammad ibn Sulayman al-Qayrati informed us, Abu Usama informed us, Burayd ibn Abdullah informed us, al-Jawzaqi said: And Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Ishaq al-Isbahani informed us, Abu al-Bakhtari Abdullah ibn Muhammad ibn Shakir informed us, Abu Usama informed us, Burayd ibn Abdullah ibn Abi Burda informed us from Abu Burda from Abu Musa, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: When the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, finished with Hunayn, he sent Abu 'Amir with the army to Awtas. He met Durayd ibn al-Simmah, and Allah killed Durayd and defeated his companions. Abu Musa said: And he sent me with Abu 'Amir. He said: Abu 'Amir was shot in his knee—a man from Bani Jusham shot him with an arrow and fixed it in his knee. So I went to him and said, 'O uncle, who shot you?' Abu 'Amir pointed to Abu Musa and said, 'That is my killer,' meaning the one who shot me. So I went to him and kept saying to him, 'Are you not ashamed? Are you not an Arab?' So he stopped, and I met him and I struck him twice. I struck him with my sword and killed him. Then I returned to Abu 'Amir and said to him, 'I have killed your man.' He said, 'Then remove this arrow.' So I removed it, and water gushed from it. He said, 'O my brother, go the Messenger of Allah and convey my greetings to him, and tell him that he says: Ask forgiveness for me.' He said, 'And Abu 'Amir appointed me over the people.' He said, 'Then he remained a short while, then he died. When I returned to the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, I entered upon him while he was in a house on a bed made of sand-filled ropes, and on it was a mat that had left marks of the sand on the back and sides of the Messenger of Allah. So I informed him of our news and the news of Abu 'Amir, and I said, 'He says: Ask forgiveness for me.' So the Messenger of Allah called for water, performed ablution, then raised his hands and said, 'O Allah, forgive 'Ubayd Abu 'Amir' until I saw the whiteness of his armpits. Then he said, 'O Allah, make him on the Day of Resurrection above many of those You created,' or 'above many of the people.' I said, 'And for me, O Messenger of Allah, ask forgiveness for me.' He said, 'O Allah, forgive 'Abdullah ibn Qays his sin and admit him on the Day of Resurrection a noble entrance.' Abu Burda said: One was for Abu 'Amir and the other for Abu Musa. It was narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim from Abu Kurayb from Abu Usamah. And in this hadith is a glad tiding for Abu al-Hasan, may Allah have mercy on him, that he is included in the Prophet's asking for forgiveness, because in it and in others there is an indication of that which is not hidden from those of understanding.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a long hadith narrative about the martyrdom of Abu 'Amir and the Prophet's prayer for him and for Abu Musa. The chain is given. The story: After the battle of Hunayn, the Prophet sent Abu 'Amir to Awtas. Abu Musa accompanied him. Abu 'Amir was shot in the knee. Abu Musa pursued the shooter, who was a non-Arab, and killed him. Then Abu Musa removed the arrow from Abu 'Amir, and water gushed out (indicating a serious wound). Abu 'Amir asked Abu Musa to convey his greetings to the Prophet and request the Prophet to ask forgiveness for him. He then died. Abu Musa returned to the Prophet, who was on a simple bed. He told him what happened. The Prophet made ablution, raised his hands and prayed for Abu 'Amir's forgiveness, and said he should be above many on the Day of Resurrection. Then Abu Musa asked the Prophet to pray for him, and the Prophet prayed for his forgiveness and a noble entrance. The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim. Ibn Asakir then comments that this hadith is a glad tiding for Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, as he is the descendant of Abu Musa, and the Prophet's prayer for Abu Musa extends to his progeny.

Key Terms
أبو عامر
أبو موسى
دريد بن الصمة
استغفار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Prophet only prayed for the most prominent companions, but here he prays for both Abu 'Amir and Abu Musa, showing his care for all.
Correction: The hadith demonstrates the Prophet's comprehensive mercy; he prayed for both companions, regardless of their status.

Checkpoint
What did Abu 'Amir ask Abu Musa to do when he was dying?
A) To bury him immediately
B) To convey his greetings to the Prophet and ask him to seek forgiveness
C) To take his weapons back to the army
D) To inform his family

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's prayer for Abu 'Amir and Abu Musa shows his deep compassion and the importance of seeking forgiveness, even in the final moments of life.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Abu 'Amir's final concern was not his wound or his life, but his forgiveness. When you face your last moments, will your greatest worry be your standing with Allah? What does that reveal about your priorities right now?
?
The Prophet prayed for Abu 'Amir and Abu Musa with humility and ablution. How often do you seek the Prophet's intercession in your own prayers? Are you truly relying on his supplication, or do you neglect this gift?
?
Abu Musa returned to find the Prophet in a humble state, yet the Prophet immediately prayed for him. When you seek forgiveness from Allah, do you approach with the same humility, or do you take His mercy for granted?

Glad Tidings for Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari
Ibn Asakir's inference of glad tidings for Abu al-Hasan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir derives a glad tiding for Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari from the hadith of Abu Musa, and the significance of this inference in defending Ash'ari theology.

Core Idea
The Prophet's prayer for Abu Musa includes his descendants, blessing Imam Abu al-Hasan.

In the final part of this passage, Ibn Asakir adds a comment that transforms the hadith into a source of honour for a later scholar. He argues that because Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari is a descendant of Abu Musa, the Prophet's prayer for forgiveness and noble entrance extends to him. This shows how the early Muslim community's legacy is tied to later theological figures.

Guided Path
1
Read the closing comment
Read the last sentence of the passage: 'And in this hadith is a glad tiding for Abu al-Hasan...'
This is Ibn Asakir's own inference.
2
Understand the connection
Recognize that Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari is a descendant of Abu Musa, so the Prophet's prayer for Abu Musa is seen to include his progeny.
This is based on a general understanding that a prayer for a person can encompass his lineage.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why Ibn Asakir highlights this: to honour Abu al-Hasan and defend his theological position by linking him to the Prophet's blessings.
This is a subtle but powerful apologetic argument.

وأخبرنا الشيخ أبو عبد الله محمد ابن الفضل الفراوي الفقيه أنا أبو بكر أحمد بن منصور بن خلف المغربي أنا أبوبكر محمد بن عبدالله بن معتمد الجوزقى أنا أبوالعباس الدغولی نا محمد بن سليمان القيراطی نا أبو أسامة نا بريد بن عبد الله قال الجوزقى وأنا أبو جعفر محمد بن الحسن بن اسحق الأصبهاني نا أبو البخترى عبد الله بن محمد بن شاكر نا أبو أسامة نا بريد بن عبد الله بن أبي بردة عن أبي بردة عن أبي موسى رضى الله عنه قال لما فرغ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من حنين بعث أبا عامر على الجيش إلى أوطاس فلقى دريد بن الصمة فقتل الله دريداً وهزم أصحابه قال أبو موسى وبعثنى مع أبي عامر قال فرمى أبو عامر في ركبته رماه رجل من بنی چشم بسهم فأثبته في ركبته فانتهيت إليه فقلت ياعم من رماك فأشار أبو عامر إلى أبي موسى فقال إن ذلك قاتلى يريد ذاك الذي رماني فأتيته وجعلت أقول له ألا تستحيى الست عربياً فكف فالتقيت أنا وهو ضربتين فضربته بالسيف فقتلته ثم رجعت إلى أبي عامر فقلت له قد قتل صاحبك قال فانزع هذا السهم فنزعته فنزا منه الماء فقال يا أخى انطلق إلى رسول الله فأقرئه منى السلام وقل له أنه يقول لك استغفر لي قال واستخلفنى أبو عامر على الناس قال فمكث يسيراً ثم أنه مات فلما رجعت إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم دخلت عليه وهو في بيت على سرير مرمل وعليه فراش قد أثر رمال السرير بظهر رسول الله وجنبيه فأخبرته بخبرنا وخبر أبي عامر فقلت يقول لك استغفر لى فدعا رسول الله له بماء فتوضا ثم رفع يديه وقال ( اللهم اغفر لعبيد أبي عامر حتى رأيت بياض ابطيه، ثم قال اللهم اجعله يوم القيامة فوق كثير ممن خلقت أو من الناس فقلت ولى يارسول الله، فاستغفر لي فقال اللهم اغفر لعبد الله بن قيس ذنبه وادخله يوم القيامة مدخلاً كريماً ) قال أبو بردة احداهما لأبي عامر والأخرى لأبي موسی، رواه البخاري ومسلم عن أبى كريب عن أبي أسامة، وفي هذا الحديث بشارة لأبي الحسن رحمه الله بدخوله في استغفار الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم إذ فيه وفى غيره إشارة إلى ذلك لا تخفى على ذوى العقول.
And the Shaykh Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Farawi al-Faqih informed us, Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Mansur ibn Khalaf al-Maghribi informed us, Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn Mu'tamad al-Jawzaqi informed us, Abu al-Abbas al-Daghuli informed us, Muhammad ibn Sulayman al-Qayrati informed us, Abu Usama informed us, Burayd ibn Abdullah informed us, al-Jawzaqi said: And Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Ishaq al-Isbahani informed us, Abu al-Bakhtari Abdullah ibn Muhammad ibn Shakir informed us, Abu Usama informed us, Burayd ibn Abdullah ibn Abi Burda informed us from Abu Burda from Abu Musa, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: When the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, finished with Hunayn, he sent Abu 'Amir with the army to Awtas. He met Durayd ibn al-Simmah, and Allah killed Durayd and defeated his companions. Abu Musa said: And he sent me with Abu 'Amir. He said: Abu 'Amir was shot in his knee—a man from Bani Jusham shot him with an arrow and fixed it in his knee. So I went to him and said, 'O uncle, who shot you?' Abu 'Amir pointed to Abu Musa and said, 'That is my killer,' meaning the one who shot me. So I went to him and kept saying to him, 'Are you not ashamed? Are you not an Arab?' So he stopped, and I met him and I struck him twice. I struck him with my sword and killed him. Then I returned to Abu 'Amir and said to him, 'I have killed your man.' He said, 'Then remove this arrow.' So I removed it, and water gushed from it. He said, 'O my brother, go the Messenger of Allah and convey my greetings to him, and tell him that he says: Ask forgiveness for me.' He said, 'And Abu 'Amir appointed me over the people.' He said, 'Then he remained a short while, then he died. When I returned to the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, I entered upon him while he was in a house on a bed made of sand-filled ropes, and on it was a mat that had left marks of the sand on the back and sides of the Messenger of Allah. So I informed him of our news and the news of Abu 'Amir, and I said, 'He says: Ask forgiveness for me.' So the Messenger of Allah called for water, performed ablution, then raised his hands and said, 'O Allah, forgive 'Ubayd Abu 'Amir' until I saw the whiteness of his armpits. Then he said, 'O Allah, make him on the Day of Resurrection above many of those You created,' or 'above many of the people.' I said, 'And for me, O Messenger of Allah, ask forgiveness for me.' He said, 'O Allah, forgive 'Abdullah ibn Qays his sin and admit him on the Day of Resurrection a noble entrance.' Abu Burda said: One was for Abu 'Amir and the other for Abu Musa. It was narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim from Abu Kurayb from Abu Usamah. And in this hadith is a glad tiding for Abu al-Hasan, may Allah have mercy on him, that he is included in the Prophet's asking for forgiveness, because in it and in others there is an indication of that which is not hidden from those of understanding.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a long hadith narrative about the martyrdom of Abu 'Amir and the Prophet's prayer for him and for Abu Musa. The chain is given. The story: After the battle of Hunayn, the Prophet sent Abu 'Amir to Awtas. Abu Musa accompanied him. Abu 'Amir was shot in the knee. Abu Musa pursued the shooter, who was a non-Arab, and killed him. Then Abu Musa removed the arrow from Abu 'Amir, and water gushed out (indicating a serious wound). Abu 'Amir asked Abu Musa to convey his greetings to the Prophet and request the Prophet to ask forgiveness for him. He then died. Abu Musa returned to the Prophet, who was on a simple bed. He told him what happened. The Prophet made ablution, raised his hands and prayed for Abu 'Amir's forgiveness, and said he should be above many on the Day of Resurrection. Then Abu Musa asked the Prophet to pray for him, and the Prophet prayed for his forgiveness and a noble entrance. The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim. Ibn Asakir then comments that this hadith is a glad tiding for Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, as he is the descendant of Abu Musa, and the Prophet's prayer for Abu Musa extends to his progeny.

بشارة
أبو الحسن
استغفار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the 'glad tiding' is a direct statement from the Prophet, but it is an inference by Ibn Asakir.
Correction: Ibn Asakir derives this glad tiding by linking Abu al-Hasan's lineage to Abu Musa, not from an explicit saying of the Prophet.

B) That Abu al-Hasan is included in the Prophet's prayer for Abu Musa
C) That Abu al-Hasan will be resurrected before others
D) That the Prophet mentioned Abu al-Hasan by name

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir interprets the Prophet's prayer for Abu Musa as encompassing his descendant Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, providing a spiritual lineage of blessing and honour.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
Ibn Asakir saw an indication in the hadith that others missed. What blind spots in your own understanding of the sources might be preventing you from seeing the deeper blessings available to you?
?
The glad tiding here is for a scholar of Ahl al-Sunna. Does your pursuit of knowledge and adherence to orthodoxy give you confidence that you are included in the Prophet's prayers, or does it lead to complacency? What must you do to truly deserve such inclusion?

The Prophet's Prayer Extends to Generations
Hadith about the Prophet's prayer covering three generations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of the hadith that the Prophet's prayer reaches a man, his child, and his grandchild, and how it supports the idea of the Prophet's blessings extending to later generations.

Core Idea
The Prophet's prayer for a person blesses his descendants for generations.

This lesson presents a short but powerful hadith from Hudhayfa (RA) that tells us the Prophet's supplication (صلاة) does not stop at the person prayed for but extends to his child and grandchild. This hadith is used by Imam Ibn Asakir to illustrate the far-reaching effect of the Prophet's blessings. Let's examine the text and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Note the chain of transmission and the content.
2
Understand the key term 'صلاة'
Recognize that in this context, صلاة means supplication or blessing, not the ritual prayer.
This is a common misunderstanding.
3
Connect to the larger argument
Consider how this hadith supports the idea that the Prophet's prayer for a person benefits his descendants, including later scholars like Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.

أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم هبة الله بن محمد بن الحصين أنا أبو طالب محمد ابن محمد بن إبراهيم بن غيلان أنا محمد ابن عبد الله بن إبراهيم الشافعي حدثني أبو يحيى الزعفرانى جعفر بن محمد بن الحسن نا الهيثم بن يمان أبو بشر نا إسماعيل بن زكريا عن مسعر عن أبي بكر بن عمرو بن عتبة عن ابن الحذيفة عن حذيفة رضى الله عنه قال صلاة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم تدرك الرجل وولده وولد ولده
The Shaykh Abu al-Qasim Hibatullah ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn informed us, Abu Talib Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Ibrahim ibn Ghaylan informed us, Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn Ibrahim al-Shafi'i informed us, Abu Yahya al-Za'farani Ja'far ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hasan narrated to me, al-Haytham ibn Yaman Abu Bishr narrated to us, Isma'il ibn Zakariyya narrated to us from Mis'ar from Abu Bakr ibn 'Amr ibn 'Utba from Ibn al-Hudhayfa from Hudhayfa, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: The prayer of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, reaches a man, his child, and the child of his child.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a short hadith narration from Hudhayfa (RA) stating that the Prophet's prayer (i.e., his supplication or blessing) encompasses a man, his child, and his child's child. The chain of transmission is given. This hadith is significant in the context because it implies that the Prophet's prayer for a person benefits his descendants, including later generations. Ibn Asakir uses this to support the idea that the prayer for Abu Musa extends to his grandson Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.

Correction: In this context, 'صلاة' means supplication or blessing.

The Prophet's prayer for a person reaches his child and grandchild, showing the enduring blessing of his supplications.

The Prophet's Prayer for Abu 'Amir and Glad Tidings for Abu al-Hasan
Ibn Asakir narrates a hadith and applies it as glad tidings for Abu al-Hasan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir uses a hadith about the Prophet's prayer for Abu 'Amir as evidence of divine favor for Abu al-Hasan.

Core Idea
A hadith about forgiveness becomes proof of honor for a later scholar.

In this passage, Ibn Asakir narrates a well-known hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim, recounting the Prophet's prayer for Abu 'Amir and his companion Abu Musa. The author then draws a remarkable conclusion: this same prayer includes Abu al-Hasan, the subject of his defense. The lesson shows how careful attention to hadith can reveal hidden blessings for later generations.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith narrative
Focus on the sequence of events after the Battle of Hunayn, including the wounding of Abu 'Amir and the Prophet's response.
The hadith is transmitted through Abu Musa al-Ash'ari.
2
Notice the Prophet's dua
Identify the specific words of the Prophet's prayer for Abu 'Amir and then for Abu Musa upon his request.
The Prophet raised his hands until the whiteness of his armpits was seen.
3
Understand Ibn Asakir's application
Recognise how Ibn Asakir applies this hadith as glad tidings for Abu al-Hasan, arguing that he is included in the Prophet's forgiveness.
Ibn Asakir says the indication is clear to those of intellect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اسحق الأصبهاني نا أبو البخترى عبد الله بن محمد بن شاكر نا أبو أسامة نا بريد بن عبد الله بن أبي بردة عن أبي بردة عن أبي موسى رضى الله عنه قال لما فرغ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من حنين بعث أبا عامر على الجيش إلى أوطاس فلقى دريد بن الصمة فقتل الله دريداً وهزم أصحابه قال أبو موسى وبعثنى مع أبي عامر قال فرمى أبو عامر في ركبته رماه رجل من بني جشم بسهم فأثبته في ركبته فانتهيت إليه فقلت ياعم من رماك فأشار أبو عامر إلى أبي موسى فقال إن ذلك قاتلى يريد ذاك الذي رماني فأتيته وجعلت أقول له ألا تستحيي الست عربياً فكف فالتقيت أنا وهو ضربتين فضربته بالسيف فقتلته ثم رجعت إلى أبي عامر فقلت له قد قتل صاحبك قال فانزع هذا السهم فنزعته فنزا منه الماء فقال يا أخى انطلق إلى رسول الله فأقرئه منى السلام وقل له أنه يقول لك استغفر لي قال واستخلفنى أبو عامر على الناس قال فمكث يسيراً ثم أنه مات فلما رجعت إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم دخلت عليه وهو في بيت على سرير مرمل وعليه فراش قد أثر رمال السرير بظهر رسول الله وجنبيه فأخبرته بخبرنا وخبر أبي عامر فقلت يقول لك استغفر لى فدعا رسول الله له بماء فتوضا ثم رفع يديه وقال ( اللهم اغفر لعبيد أبي عامر حتى رأيت بياض ابطيه، ثم قال اللهم اجعله يوم القيامة فوق كثير ممن خلقت أو من الناس فقلت ولى يارسول الله، فاستغفر لي فقال اللهم اغفر لعبد الله بن قيس ذنبه وادخله يوم القيامة مدخلاً كريماً ) قال أبو بردة احداهما لأبي عامر والأخرى لأبي موسی، رواه البخاري ومسلم عن أبى كريب عن أبي أسامة، وفي هذا الحديث بشارة لأبي الحسن رحمه الله بدخوله في استغفار الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم إذ فيه وفى غيره إشارة إلى ذلك لا تخفى على ذوى العقول.
Isḥāq al-Aṣbahānī narrated to us: Abū al-Bakhtarī ʿAbd Allāh ibn Muḥammad ibn Shākir narrated to us: Abū Usāma narrated to us: Burayd ibn ʿAbd Allāh ibn Abī Burda from Abī Burda from Abī Mūsā (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: When the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) finished with Ḥunayn, he sent Abū ʿĀmir over the army to Awtās. He met Durayd ibn al-Ṣimma, Allah killed Durayd and defeated his companions. Abū Mūsā said: He sent me with Abū ʿĀmir. He said: Abū ʿĀmir was shot in his knee—a man from Banī Jashm shot him with an arrow and lodged it in his knee. I went to him and said, 'Uncle, who shot you?' Abū ʿĀmir pointed to Abū Mūsā and said, 'That one is my killer,' meaning the one who shot me. I went to him and kept saying, 'Are you not ashamed? Are you not an Arab?' So he stopped, and I met him and he exchanged two blows. I struck him with the sword and killed him. Then I returned to Abū ʿĀmir and said, 'I have killed your companion.' He said, 'Remove this arrow.' So I removed it, and water came out of it. He said, 'O brother, go to the Messenger of Allah, convey my greeting of peace, and tell him: He says to you, ask forgiveness for me.' He said: Abū ʿĀmir appointed me over the people. He said: He stayed a short while, then he died. When I returned to the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him), I entered upon him while he was in a house on a bed with a rope frame, and on it a mattress that had left marks of the rope’s weaving on the back and sides of the Messenger of Allah. I informed him of our news and the news of Abū ʿĀmir, and said, 'He tells you to ask forgiveness for me.' So the Messenger of Allah called for water, performed ablution, then raised his hands and said, 'O Allah, forgive ʿUbayd Abī ʿĀmir [i.e., Abū ʿĀmir]' until I saw the whiteness of his armpits. Then he said, 'O Allah, make him on the Day of Resurrection above many of those You have created, or of the people.' I said, 'And for me, O Messenger of Allah, ask forgiveness.' He said, 'O Allah, forgive ʿAbd Allāh ibn Qays his sin and admit him on the Day of Resurrection a noble entrance.' Abū Burda said: One of these [supplications] was for Abū ʿĀmir and the other for Abū Mūsā. Al-Bukhārī and Muslim narrated it from Abū Kurayb from Abī Usāma. In this ḥadīth is a glad tiding for Abū al-Ḥasan (may Allah have mercy on him) of his inclusion in the forgiveness-asking of the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him), for in it and in others there is an indication to that which is not hidden from people of intellect.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a hadith narration followed by the author's editorial comment. The hadith is transmitted through a chain from Abū Mūsā al-Ashʿarī (رضي الله عنه) and recounts events after the battle of Ḥunayn. The Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) sent Abū ʿĀmir on a military expedition to Awtās, where he was wounded in the knee by an arrow. Abū Mūsā describes how he killed the attacker at Abū ʿĀmir's request, then removed the arrow. Abū ʿĀmir asked Abū Mūsā to convey his request for the Prophet's forgiveness. When Abū Mūsā returned and reported this, the Prophet performed ablution, raised his hands, and prayed for Abū ʿĀmir's forgiveness and exaltation on the Day of Resurrection. Abū Mūsā then asked the Prophet to pray for him as well, and the Prophet did so. The hadith concludes with Abū Burda noting that one prayer was for Abū ʿĀmir and the other for Abū Mūsā. The author, Ibn ʿAsākir, then adds that this hadith is a glad tiding for Abū al-Ḥasan (referring to the subject of his biographical defense) because it shows that he is included in the Prophet's prayer for forgiveness, either through this hadith or through other indications that are clear to those of understanding. The author is using this hadith as evidence to support the virtue and divine favor upon Abū al-Ḥasan, likely in the context of defending him against accusations.

Key Terms
استغفار
بشارة
أبي الحسن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the glad tidings apply only to Abū ʿĀmir.
Correction: Ibn ʿAsākir applies them to Abū al-Ḥasan through inclusion in the Prophet's forgiveness, as indicated in the hadith and other evidences.

Checkpoint
Who did the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) pray for forgiveness first in this hadith?
A) Abū Mūsā
B) Abū ʿĀmir
C) Abū al-Ḥasan
D) Durayd ibn al-Ṣimma

Key Takeaway
Ibn ʿAsākir uses the Prophet's prayer for Abū ʿĀmir as evidence that Abū al-Ḥasan is included in the Prophet's forgiveness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet’s prayer for a companion can be a sign of mercy for a scholar centuries later, could it also be a sign for you? Do you live as though his prayer might cover your sins? What would change if you truly believed you are included in his concern for the Ummah?
?
Abu Amir’s last wish was for the Prophet to ask forgiveness for him. If you knew you were dying, what would be your last request from the Prophet? Are you living now in a way that would make that request sincere?
?
Ibn Asakir saw glad tidings hidden in a hadith for a specific person. What hidden signs of Allah’s mercy toward you might you be ignoring? Will you look for them today in the words of the Prophet?

Abu Musa's Beautiful Quran Recitation
Report on Abu Musa's voice surpassing musical instruments in beauty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the virtue of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari's Quran recitation and the lesson that the beauty of the Quran surpasses worldly music.

Core Idea
The beauty of Quran recitation surpasses all musical instruments.

This lesson presents a historical report about the companion Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. Through an eyewitness account, we learn that his recitation of the Quran was so beautiful that it exceeded the pleasure of musical instruments. The passage highlights the superiority of divine speech over worldly entertainment.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic narration once, then read the literal translation. Notice the chain of narrators and the final statement.
The chain shows the report's authenticity.
2
Identify the three musical instruments
Find the three instruments mentioned: mizmar (flute), tunbur (tambourine), sanaj (cymbal). Understand that these were common instruments of the time.
3
Reflect on the comparison
Think about why Abu Uthman said he never heard a more beautiful sound than Abu Musa's voice. What does this tell us about the status of Quranic recitation?
The comparison elevates the recitation above worldly music.
4
Understand the lesson
The lesson is not about permitting musical instruments, but about the virtue of beautiful Quran recitation. The companions appreciated beauty in recitation.
Avoid the misconception that this equates Quran with music.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم هبة الله بن محمد بن عبدالواحد الشيباني أنا أبو طالب محمد بن محمد بن إبراهيم بن غيلان الهمذاني، أنا أبوبكر محمد بن عبد الله بن إبراهيم الشافعي نا عبد الله ابن أحمد بن حنبل نا أبي نا معتمر عن أبيه عن أبي عثمان قال ما سمعت مزماراً ولا طنبوراً ولا صنجاً أحسن من صوت أبي موسى الأشعرى رضى الله عنه كان ليصلي بنا فنود أنه قرأ البقرة من حسن صوته.
The shaykh Abu al-Qasim Hibatullah ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Wahid al-Shaybani informed us, he said: Abu Talib Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Ibrahim ibn Ghaylan al-Hamadhani narrated to us, he said: Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn Ibrahim al-Shafi'i narrated to us, he said: Abdullah ibn Ahmad ibn Hanbal narrated to us, he said: my father narrated to me, he said: Mu'tamir narrated to us from his father from Abu Uthman who said: I have never heard a flute, nor a tambourine, nor a cymbal more beautiful than the voice of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with him. He used to lead us in prayer, and we would think that he was reciting Surah al-Baqarah due to the beauty of his voice.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a biographical report transmitted through a chain of narrators. It describes an eyewitness account from Abu Uthman, who states that he never heard any musical instrument—specifically a flute (mizmar), a tambourine (tunbur), or a cymbal (sanaj)—that surpassed the beauty of the voice of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari (may Allah be pleased with him) when he recited the Quran. The narrator remarks that when Abu Musa led them in prayer, they would imagine he was reciting Surah al-Baqarah because of the melodious quality of his voice. This report serves to highlight the virtue of Abu Musa and the beauty of Quranic recitation, which is preferred over worldly music.

Key Terms
Mizmar
Tunbur
Sanaj
Abu Musa al-Ash'ari

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that this report permits musical instruments because it compares the Quranic voice to them.
Correction: The report is only praising the voice, not endorsing instruments. It highlights the virtue of beautiful recitation, not the permissibility of music.

Checkpoint

B) Flute, tambourine, cymbal
C) Lute, flute, tambourine
D) Only flute

Key Takeaway
The beauty of Quran recitation is superior to musical instruments, and it should inspire reverence, not imitation of music.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the voice of a human companion could surpass musical instruments, how much more should the Quran itself impact your heart? Examine your attachment to music versus Quran recitation. What specific step will you take today to prioritize the Quran over worldly sounds?
?
Abu Musa's recitation was so beautiful that listeners felt he was reciting a long surah like al-Baqarah. When you recite Quran, does time seem to fly? If not, what is missing in your connection to the Quran? Commit to one practical improvement in your recitation this week.
?
This narration comes through a long chain of trustworthy narrators—people dedicated to preserving Allah's words. Are you just as careful about the sources of your knowledge? Are you learning Islam from reliable teachers and texts? Write down one concrete action to verify and strengthen your Islamic learning.

Ali's Assessments of the Companions' Knowledge
Ali describes the scholarly attributes of six companions and himself.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ali (RA) evaluated the knowledge and traits of several prominent companions, highlighting their unique strengths and limitations.

Core Idea
Each companion had a distinct relationship with knowledge, as assessed by Ali.

In this passage, a group of companions asked Ali (RA) to describe the knowledge of several notable figures. His responses reveal a nuanced understanding of each person's scholarly capacity and spiritual state. As you read, notice how Ali’s assessments are not merely factual but also reflect deep insight into character.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the narrator's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
This is a hadith-like narration with a chain of transmission.
2
Notice the question-and-answer format
The companions ask Ali about specific individuals, and he responds concisely. Pay attention to the structure: each answer begins with the companion's name.
The questions are implied by the answers.
3
Identify the specific trait for each companion
For each companion mentioned, identify the exact phrase Ali uses. Consider what it reveals about that person's knowledge or character.
Some evaluations are straightforward, others metaphorical.
4
Reflect on the diversity of knowledge among the companions
Think about how these different evaluations show that the companions had varied strengths. Why might Ali highlight these differences?
This connects to the broader theme of knowledge in Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم إسماعيل بن أحمد بن السمرقندي أنا محمد ابن أحمد بن على بن الحسن بن أبي عثمان وأبوطاهر أحمد بن محمد بن إبراهيم القصارى ح وأخبرنا الشيخ أبو عبد الله محمد بن أحمد ابن القصارى أنا أبى قالا أنا أبو القسم إسماعيل بن الحسن بن عبد الله العسكري نا الحسين بن إسماعيل المحاملي نا الحسن بن محمد بن الصباح نا محمد بن عبيد نا الأعمش عن عمرو بن مرة عن أبى البختري قال أتينا علياً رضى الله عنه فسألناه عن أصحاب محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم قال أيهم قلنا عن عبد الله قال ( علم القرآن والسنة ثم انتهى وكفى به علما ) قلنا أبو موسى قال ( صبغ في العلم صبغة ثم خرج منه قلنا حذيفة قال ( اعلم أصحاب محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم بالمنافقين) قلنا عمار قال ) مؤمن نسى إن ذكرته ذكر ) قلنا أبو ذر قال ( وعى علماً ثم عجز فيه ) قلنا سلمان قال ( أدرك العلم الأول والآخر بحر لا يدرك قعره منا أهل البيت ) قلنا أخبرنا عن نفسك يا أمير المؤمنين قال ( كنت إذا سألت أعطيت وإذا سكنت انتدبت)،
The shaykh Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Ahmad ibn al-Samarqandi informed us, he said: Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Ali ibn al-Hasan ibn Abi Uthman and Abu Tahir Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Qassari [ح] and the shaykh Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn al-Qassari informed us, he said: my father narrated to us, they both said: Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn al-Hasan ibn Abdullah al-Askari narrated to us, he said: al-Husayn ibn Isma'il al-Mahamili narrated to us, he said: al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn al-Sabah narrated to us, he said: Muhammad ibn Ubayd narrated to us, he said: al-A'mash narrated to us from Amr ibn Murra from Abu al-Bakhtari who said: We came to Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) and asked him about the companions of Muhammad (peace be upon him). He asked: 'Which one?' We said: 'About Abdullah (Ibn Mas'ud).' He said: 'He learned the Quran and the Sunnah, then he stopped, and it sufficed him as knowledge.' We said: 'Abu Musa.' He said: 'He was dipped in knowledge once, then he came out of it.' We said: 'Hudhayfah.' He said: 'The most knowledgeable of the companions of Muhammad (peace be upon him) about the hypocrites.' We said: 'Ammar.' He said: 'A believer who forgets; if you remind him, he remembers.' We said: 'Abu Dharr.' He said: 'He absorbed knowledge, but he was incapable in it.' We said: 'Salman.' He said: 'He attained the first and last knowledge; an ocean whose depth cannot be reached; he is from us, the Ahl al-Bayt.' We said: 'Inform us about yourself, O Commander of the Believers.' He said: 'If I was asked, I was given, and if I remained silent, I was summoned.'
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is a report from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) where he evaluates the knowledge of several prominent companions. It is a classification of each person's specific scholarly trait. For Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, he praises his comprehensive knowledge of Quran and Sunnah and his contentment. For Abu Musa, he says he was 'dipped in knowledge' (sabgha fil 'ilm sabgha) but then came out of it—perhaps indicating he learned much but did not remain exclusive to it. Hudhayfah is distinguished for his knowledge of the hypocrites. Ammar is described as a believer who forgets but reminds. Abu Dharr is seen as knowledgeable but unable to act fully. Salman is praised as having vast knowledge like an ocean and being from the Ahl al-Bayt (spiritually). Finally, Ali describes himself as one who gives answers when asked and is summoned when silent, indicating his readiness to teach.

Key Terms
علم
صبغة
وعى
أهل البيت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Ali's statement about Abu Musa 'came out of it' is a criticism of his knowledge.
Correction: It likely means he did not remain in that state of exclusive dipping, not that his knowledge was deficient.

Checkpoint
According to Ali, who is the most knowledgeable of the Prophet's companions about the hypocrites?
A) Abu Musa
B) Hudhayfah
C) Ammar
D) Abdullah

Key Takeaway
Ali’s descriptions reveal the diversity of knowledge and character among the Prophet’s companions, each with unique strengths.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you learn a new Islamic teaching, do you stop like Ibn Mas'ud, content with what you have, or do you become like Abu Musa, dipped briefly and then moving on? What would it take for you to go deeper?
?
Ali described Ammar as a believer who forgets and needs reminding. Is there a duty of faith you have neglected? Who can remind you, and will you accept their reminder with humility?
?
Ali said of himself: 'If I was asked, I was given; if I remained silent, I was summoned.' Do you feel prepared to answer when someone asks you about your faith, or do you stay silent out of ignorance? What one step can you take this week to be more ready?

Four Judges and Six Muftis of the Umma
Ali ibn al-Madini lists the four judges and six muftis among the companions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the recognized judges (qudat) and muftis among the companions according to the renowned hadith scholar Ali ibn al-Madini.

Core Idea
The early community recognized four judges and six muftis among the companions.

This lesson presents a concise list from Ali ibn al-Madini, identifying the companions who served as judges and those who issued legal verdicts. The list shows specialized roles among the early Muslims and highlights the authority of these companions in jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the isnad (chain of transmission) that records this statement, showing its scholarly authority.
The isnaad adds credibility to the report.
2
Identify the two lists
The passage contains two enumerations: the four judges and the six muftis. Note who is included in each list and the overlap between them.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why these particular companions were singled out for these roles. This tells us about the early community's recognition of expertise in judicial and legal matters.
Not all judges were caliphs; Zayd and Abu Musa were not caliphs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخبرنا الشيخ أبو عبد الله محمد بن الفضل أنا أبوبكر أحمد بن الحسين الحافظ أنا محمد بن عبدالله الحافظ أنا الحسين بن محمد ابن اسحق أنا محمد بن أحمد بن البراء قال سمعت على بن عبد الله المدينى يقول : كان يقال قضاة هذه الأمة أربعة عمر بن الخطاب وعلى بن أبي طالب وزيد بن ثابت وأبو موسى الأشعرى رضى الله عنهم قال على: و كان الفتيا في أصحاب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في ستة : عمر وعلى وعبد الله وزيد وأبى موسى وأبي بن كعب رضى الله عنهم .
The shaykh Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl informed us, he said: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Hafiz narrated to us, he said: Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Hafiz narrated to us, he said: al-Husayn ibn Muhammad ibn Ishaq narrated to us, he said: Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn al-Bara' narrated to us, he said: I heard Ali ibn Abdullah al-Madini say: It used to be said: The judges of this nation are four: Umar ibn al-Khattab, Ali ibn Abi Talib, Zayd ibn Thabit, and Abu Musa al-Ash'ari (may Allah be pleased with them). Ali (ibn al-Madini) said: And the giving of fatwa among the companions of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was among six: Umar, Ali, Abdullah (Ibn Mas'ud), Zayd, Abu Musa, and Ubayy ibn Ka'b (may Allah be pleased with them).
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage records the statement of the renowned hadith critic Ali ibn al-Madini (d. 234/849). He transmits a saying that the recognized judges (qudat) of the Islamic community among the companions are four: Umar, Ali, Zayd, and Abu Musa. He adds that the specialists in issuing legal verdicts (fatwa) were six: the same four plus Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and Ubayy ibn Ka'b. This highlights the established authority of these companions in jurisprudence and judicial matters.

Key Terms
قضاة
فتيا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that only the caliphs served as judges during the time of the Prophet and early caliphate.
Correction: The list includes non-caliphs like Zayd ibn Thabit and Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, showing that judicial authority was based on knowledge and expertise, not just political leadership.

Checkpoint

B) Umar, Ali, Zayd, Abu Musa
C) Umar, Ali, Abdullah, Zayd
D) Umar, Ali, Abu Musa, Ubayy

Key Takeaway
Ali ibn al-Madini's list preserves the early Muslim community's recognition of specific companions as authoritative judges and muftis, emphasizing that expertise in law was the key criterion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you seek guidance on religious matters, do you consciously turn to the recognized scholars and authorities of Islam, or do you rely on your own reasoning? Examine your practice—are you truly following the legacy of these companions who dedicated themselves to knowledge?
?
These companions were singled out for their expertise, not their political power. Do you value knowledge over status in your own life? When choosing whom to learn from, do you prioritize their learning and piety or their popularity and fame?
?
The early community agreed on who the authorities were. Are you part of a community that recognizes and submits to knowledgeable scholars, or do you isolate yourself from communal guidance? What steps will you take to connect with those who carry the legacy of these companions?

The Six Companions of Qada
A report enumerating six companions known for qada.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will know which six companions were known for qada (judicial rulings) and understand the significance of this list.

Core Idea
Six companions formed the core of Islamic judicial knowledge.

This lesson presents a brief but important report from Masruq through al-Sha'bi, listing the six companions most associated with qada—judicial decision-making. Though short, this list carries weight because it comes from an early authority and shows which figures the first generations looked to for legal guidance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage with chain
Read the Arabic passage once, noticing the long chain of transmission. Then read the translation. Recognize that such chains establish credibility.
The chain includes well-known narrators like al-Bayhaqi and al-Sha'bi.
2
Identify the six companions
List the six names given: Umar, Ali, Abdullah (Ibn Mas'ud), Ubayy (ibn Ka'b), Zayd (ibn Thabit), and Abu Musa (al-Ash'ari). Note the order.
3
Consider why these six
Think about why these particular companions were recognized for qada. They were known for deep knowledge of the Qur'an and Sunna, and many served as judges or gave fatwas.
This list overlaps significantly with the companions known for ifta' (fatwa).
4
Reflect on the significance
Understand that early Muslims preserved such lists to identify authoritative sources of Islamic law. The consistency of this list across multiple chains reinforces its reliability.
Compare to the list of muftis from other sources.
