The Slander Against Al-Ash'ari in Nishapur
Al-Qushayri narrates the cursing of al-Ash'ari and the heretics' slander.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical context of the cursing of al-Ash'ari and how his opponents falsely attributed blameworthy doctrines to him.

Core Idea
False accusations against al-Ash'ari were a desperate ploy by heretics facing the Sultan's justice.

This lesson presents a dramatic episode from Islamic history: the cursing of Imam al-Ash'ari from the pulpits of Nishapur. Al-Qushayri, a leading scholar, recounts how the enemies of the Ash'ari school, unable to withstand the Sultan's support for Sunni orthodoxy, resorted to slander. As you read the passage, notice how al-Qushayri frames the event within divine decree and highlights the utter falsehood of their claims.

Guided Path
1
Read the historical context
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get a sense of the narrative. Note the preamble about divine decree and the description of the trial in Nishapur.
The passage is a letter from al-Qushayri to scholars, so it has an official tone.
2
Identify the key figures
The passage mentions Imam al-Ash'ari, the Sultan Tughrilbek, and the heretics (innovators). Understand their roles: al-Ash'ari is the reviver of the Sunna, the Sultan is the enforcer, and the heretics are the opponents.
3
Analyze the heretics' plot
Focus on the section where the heretics, distressed by the Sultan's actions, devise a plan. They slander al-Ash'ari by attributing false doctrines to him. The text emphasizes that these doctrines are not found in any of his books.
This is the core of the lesson: the defense of al-Ash'ari's orthodoxy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رفعها عبدالكريم بن هوازن القشيري إلى العلماء الاعلام بجميع بلاد الإسلام أما بعد فان الله إذا أراد أمرا قدره فمن ذا الذي أمسك ما سيره، أو قدم ما أخره أو عارض حكمه فغيره، أو غلبه على أمره فقهره كلا بل هو الله الواحد القهار الماجد الجبار ومما ظهر ببلد نيسابور من قضايا التقدير في مفتتح سنة خمس وأربعين وأربعمائة من الهجرة ما دعا أهل الدين إلى شق صدور صبرهم وكشف قناع ضرهم، بل ظلت الملة الحنيفية تشكو غليلها وتبدى عويلها، وتنصب غزائر رحمة الله على من يسمع شكوها، وتصغى ملائكة السماء حين تندب شجوها ذلك مما أحدث من لعن إمام الدين وسراج ذوى اليقين محیی السنة وقامع البدعة وناصر الحق وناصح الخلق الزكي الرضى أبى الحسن الأشعري قدس الله روحه وسقى بماء الرحمة ضريحه، وهو الذي ذب عن الدين بأوضح حجج وسلك فى قمع المعتزلة وسائر أنواع المبتدعة أبين منهج واستنفد عمره في النصح عن الحق، وأورث المسلمين بعد وفاته كتبه الشاهدة بالصدق .. ولما من الله الكريم على الإسلام بزمان السلطان المعظم المحكم بالقوة السماوية فى رقاب الأمم الملك الأجل شاهنشاه يمين خليفة الله، وغياث عباد الله طغرلبك أبي طالب محمد بن ميكائيل .. وقام باحياء السنة والمناضلة عن الملة حتى لم يبق من أصناف المبتدعة حزبا إلا سل لاستئصالهم سيفا، عضبا وأذاقهم ذلا وخسفا وعقب لآثارهم نسفا حرجت صدور أهل البدع عن تحمل هذه النقم وضاق صبرهم عن مقاساة هذا الألم، ومنوا بلعن أنفسهم على رؤس الاشهاد بألسنتهم وضاقت عليهم الأرض بما رحبت بانفرادهم بالوقوع في مهواة محنتهم، فسولت لهم انفسهم أمرا فظنوا انهم بنوع تلبيس وضرب تدليس يجدون لعسرهم يسرا فسعوا إلى عالى مجلس السلطان المعظم بنوع نميمة ونسبوا الأشعرى إلى مذاهب ذميمة، وحكوا عنه مقالات لا يوجد في كتبه منها حرف ولم ير في المقالات المصنفة لمين الموافقين والمخالفين من وقت الأوائل إلى زماننا هذا لشيء منها
Abd al-Karim ibn Hawazin al-Qushayri raised it to the eminent scholars in all lands of Islam. To proceed: Indeed, when God wills a matter, He decrees it. So who is there that can hold back what He has set in motion, or bring forward what He has delayed, or oppose His judgment and change it, or overcome Him in His affair and overpower Him? No, rather He is God, the One, the Subduer, the Majestic, the Compeller. Among the decreed events that appeared in the city of Nishapur at the beginning of the year 445 AH was what called the people of religion to rend the fabric of their patience and unveil the veil of their harm. Rather, the hanifite community complained of its distress and displayed its wailing, setting the water skins of God's mercy upon those who hear its complaint, and the angels of heaven incline when it laments its grief. That was due to what was initiated of cursing the Imam of the religion, the lamp of the people of certainty, the reviver of the Sunna, the suppressor of innovation, the supporter of truth, the advisor to creation, the pure and pleasing Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, may God sanctify his soul and water his grave with the water of mercy. He is the one who defended religion with the clearest proofs and pursued in suppressing the Mu'tazila and all types of innovators the clearest path. He spent his life in sincere advice for the truth, and bequeathed to the Muslims after his death his books that testify to the truth. And when God the Generous bestowed upon Islam the time of the great sultan, the ruler with heavenly authority over the necks of nations, the most noble king, shahanshah, the right hand of God's caliph, the succor of God's servants, Tughrilbek Abu Talib Muhammad ibn Mika'il... and he undertook to revive the Sunna and struggle for the religion until there remained no sect of innovators except he drew a sharp sword to uproot them, and made them taste humiliation and disgrace, and obliterated their traces—then the breasts of the people of innovation were straitened from bearing these afflictions, and their patience could not endure this pain. They wished for cursing themselves on the heads of witnesses with their own tongues, and the earth felt straitened upon them despite its breadth due to their being alone in falling into the abyss of their trial. So their souls suggested to them an idea, and they thought that by a type of obfuscation and a kind of deceit they would find ease in their difficulty. So they went to the lofty court of the great sultan with a type of slander, and they attributed to al-Ash'ari blameworthy doctrines, and they related about him statements of which not a single letter is found in his books, and nothing of them is seen in the authored works (whether of supporters or opponents) from the time of the early ones to our own time.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a detailed narrative of the events that prompted al-Qushayri to write his treatise. It begins with a preamble affirming God's absolute power and decree, establishing that whatever happens is by His will. Then al-Qushayri describes what appeared in Nishapur in the year 445 AH: a trial that caused the religious people great distress. The trial was the cursing of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, whom al-Qushayri eulogizes as the reviver of the Sunna, suppressor of innovation, and defender of the faith with clear proofs. He notes that al-Ash'ari spent his life in sincere advice and left behind truthful books. Then the narrative moves to the political context: God blessed Islam with the reign of Sultan Tughrilbek, who vigorously revived the Sunna and suppressed all sects of innovators with force, causing them humiliation. Because of this, the innovators became desperate; they wished they could curse themselves publicly, but instead they devised a plot. Thinking they could ease their difficulty through obfuscation and deceit, they went to the sultan's court and slandered al-Ash'ari, attributing to him blameworthy doctrines and claiming he said things that are not found in any of his books, whether in the works of his supporters or opponents, from the earliest times to the present. Thus al-Qushayri emphasizes the falsehood of their accusations.

Key Terms
الأشعري
السلطان طغرلبك
المعتزلة
المبتدعة
لعن
نيسابور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That al-Ash'ari held heretical doctrines such as those attributed to him by his opponents.
Correction: Al-Qushayri states that not a single letter of these accusations is found in any of al-Ash'ari's books or in the works of any scholars from the earliest times to the present, proving their falsehood.

Checkpoint
According to al-Qushayri, what did the heretics do when they could not bear the sultan's support for Sunnism?
A) They openly declared repentance
B) They slandered al-Ash'ari before the sultan, claiming he taught heretical doctrines
C) They left Nishapur
D) They wrote letters to the caliph

Key Takeaway
The false accusations against Imam al-Ash'ari were a desperate attempt by heretics to undermine the Sunni revival led by Sultan Tughrilbek, but al-Qushayri proves their baselessness by noting the complete absence of such statements in al-Ash'ari's works.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear negative claims about a scholar of Ahl al-Sunna, do you immediately investigate their books and the works of their peers to verify the truth, or do you passively accept such claims? What would al-Qushayri's response teach you about your own duty in such situations? This week, what specific claim about a scholar can you verify by going to primary sources?
?
The heretics in Nishapur were so constrained by the truth that they resorted to slander and deceit. Where in your own life are you tempted to distort or hide the truth because it pressures your desires or comfort? Will you confess that struggle to God and resolve to stand with the truth even when it is difficult?
?
Al-Qushayri wrote this account to defend the reputation of a deceased imam. Is there a person—living or dead—whom you have wronged by spreading or believing false accusations? What practical step will you take this week to correct that wrong, whether by seeking forgiveness or by setting the record straight?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
intermediate
5 min
Al-Ash'ari's Creed and the False Accusations
Ibn Asakir enumerates al-Ash'ari's beliefs and declares his critics false.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core beliefs of al-Ash'ari that caused opposition and why Ibn Asakir considers the accusations baseless.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's beliefs were fully in line with Ahl al-Sunnah; his critics were false.

Ibn Asakir begins by rejecting the criticisms of al-Ash'ari as pure fabrication. He then lists the specific doctrines that provoked opposition—affirmation of divine decree, God's attributes, uncreated Quran, vision of God, and effective will—all of which are standard Sunni positions. This lesson examines those beliefs and Ibn Asakir's assertion that al-Ash'ari's orthodoxy is undeniable.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once to appreciate Ibn Asakir's rhetorical style. Then read the translation.
Notice the strong language: 'fabrication of forgery and slander'.
2
Identify the listed beliefs
Find the specific beliefs of al-Ash'ari mentioned. There are about eight distinct items. List them in your mind.
These are the core points of contention.
3
Understand Ibn Asakir's defense
Ibn Asakir argues that al-Ash'ari's books are widespread and his school is accepted by Ahl al-Sunnah. Why does that refute the accusations?
He also quotes Quran 9:32 to support divine protection of truth.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Ibn Asakir concludes this section by stating he has shown al-Ash'ari's innocence on four specific issues. Why is this important for the reader?
It sets up the second part of the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكاية ولا وصف، بل كل ذلك تصوير بتزوير وبهتان بغیر تقدیر. وما نقموا من الأشعرى إلا أنه قال بإثبات القدر الله خيره وشره نفعه وضره، وإثبات صفات الجلال الله من قدرته وعلمه وإرادته وحياته وبقائه وسمعه وبصره وكلامه ووجهه ويده وأن القرآن كلام الله غير مخلوق وأنه تعالى موجود تجوز رؤيته وأن إرادته نافذة فى مراداته وما لا يخفى من مسائل الأصول التي تخالف طرقه طرق المعتزلة والمجسمة فيها .. معاشر المسلمين الغياث الغياث سعوا في ابطال الدين وراموا هدم قواعد المسلمين وهيهات هيهات ( يريدون ليطفئوا نور الله بأفواههم ويأبى الله إلا أن يتم نوره ) وقد وعد الله للحق نصره وظهوره وللباطل محقه وثبوره إلا أن كتب الأشعرى في الآفاق مبثوثة ومذاهبه عند أهل السنة من الفريقين معروفة ومشهورة فمن وصفه بالبدعة علم أنه غير محق في دعواه وجميع أهل السنة خصمه فيما افتراه - ثم ذكر أربع مسائل شنع بها عليه وبين براءة ساحته فيما نسب منها إليه ثم قال - ولما ظهر ابتداء هذه الفتنة بنيسابور وانتشر في الأفاق خبره وعظم على قلوب كافة المسلمين من أهل السنة والجماعة أمره، ولم يبعد أن يخامر قلوب بعض أهل السلامة والوداعة توهم في بعض هذه المسائل ان لعل الامام أبا الحسن على بن اسمعيل الأشعري رحمه الله قال ببعض هذه المقالات في بعض كتبه ولقد قيل ( من يسمع يخل أثبتنا هذه التصول في شرح هذه الحالة وأوضحنا صورة الأمر بذكر هذه الجملة ليضرب كل من أهل السنة إذا وقف عليها بسهمه في الانتصار لدين الله من دعاء يخلصه واهتمام يصدقه وكل عن قلوبنا بالاستماع إلى هذه القصة يحمله، بل ثواب من الله على التوجع بذلك يستوجبه، والله غالب على أمره وله الحمد على ما يمضيه من أحكامه ويبرمه ويقضيه من افعاله فيما يؤخره ويقدمه، وصلواته على سيدنا المصطفى وعلى آله وسلم ولا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله العلى العظيم .
A narrative and a description, rather all of that is a fabrication of forgery and slander without measure. And they only criticized al-Ash'ari because he affirmed al-qadar (divine decree) – Allah, its good and its evil, its benefit and its harm – and affirmed the attributes of majesty of Allah: His power, His knowledge, His will, His life, His permanence, His hearing, His sight, His speech, His face, and His hand; and that the Qur'an is the speech of Allah, uncreated; and that He, exalted, exists and is permissible to be seen; and that His will is effective in His objects of will; and other such foundational issues that differ from the ways of the Mu'tazila and the Mujassima in them. O community of Muslims! Help! Help! They have striven to nullify the religion and sought to demolish the foundations of the Muslims, but far be it, far be it (they intend to extinguish the light of Allah with their mouths, but Allah refuses except to perfect His light). Allah has promised victory and manifestation to the truth, and effacement and destruction to falsehood. However, the books of al-Ash'ari are scattered in the horizons and his schools are known and famous among Ahl al-Sunnah of both groups. So whoever describes him as innovation knows that he is not truthful in his claim, and all Ahl al-Sunnah are his opponents in what he has fabricated. Then he mentioned four issues by which they reviled him, and he clarified his innocence in what was attributed to him. Then he said: When this fitna first appeared in Nishapur and its news spread in the horizons, and its matter became great upon the hearts of all Muslims from Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, it is not unlikely that there might enter the hearts of some people of safety and gentleness a doubt that perhaps Imam Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Isma'il al-Ash'ari (may Allah have mercy on him) said some of these statements in some of his books. And it has been said: 'Whoever hears, he thinks.' We have established these principles in explaining this situation and we have clarified the image of the matter by mentioning this statement, so that every person of Ahl al-Sunnah, when he comes across it, may take his share in defending the religion of Allah – from a sincere supplication and a truthful concern – and everyone from our hearts, by listening to this story, carries it. Rather, he deserves a reward from Allah for feeling pain about that. And Allah is dominant over His affair, and praise be to Him for the judgments He enacts and completes and the actions He decrees in what He delays and advances. And His blessings be upon our Master the Chosen one and upon his family and peace. And there is no power nor strength except with Allah, the Most High, the Magnificent.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a defense of al-Ash'ari by Ibn Asakir. It begins by stating that the criticisms of al-Ash'ari are baseless fabrications. It then lists the core beliefs of al-Ash'ari that provoked opposition: affirming divine decree (qadar) with its good and evil, affirming God's attributes (power, knowledge, will, life, permanence, hearing, sight, speech, face, and hands), the uncreatedness of the Quran, the possibility of seeing God in the afterlife, and the effectiveness of God's will. These principles, Ibn Asakir notes, conflict with the methods of the Mu'tazila and the Mujassima. He then cries out to the Muslim community for help, accusing the enemies of trying to destroy religion, and quotes the Quranic verse (9:32) about those who seek to extinguish Allah's light. He asserts that Allah has promised victory to truth and destruction to falsehood. Despite the attacks, al-Ash'ari's books are widespread and his school is well-known among both groups of Ahl al-Sunnah (likely the Ash'aris and Maturidis, or the Hanbalis and Ash'aris). Whoever calls him an innovator is false, and all Ahl al-Sunnah oppose that accuser. Ibn Asakir then mentions that he has listed four specific issues used to vilify al-Ash'ari and has shown his innocence. He describes the beginning of the fitna in Nishapur, its spread, and its effect on the hearts of Muslims. He explains that he wrote this clarification to allow every Muslim to participate in defending the religion, hoping for reward from Allah. The passage concludes with praise and blessings.

Key Terms
أبو الحسن الأشعري
القدر
صفات الله
القرآن غير مخلوق
رؤية الله
المعتزلة
المجسمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think al-Ash'ari deviated from Ahl al-Sunnah by introducing innovation.
Correction: Ibn Asakir shows that al-Ash'ari's beliefs are exactly those of Ahl al-Sunnah, and his critics are the ones fabricating lies.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Asakir, which of the following is NOT among the beliefs of al-Ash'ari mentioned?
A) The Quran is uncreated
B) God can be seen in the afterlife
C) God has a physical body
D) Divine decree includes good and evil

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's creed, as defended by Ibn Asakir, is fully in line with Sunni orthodoxy, and accusations of innovation are baseless.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever repeated an accusation against a scholar or fellow Muslim without verifying its truth, based only on what others said? This lesson shows how slander can be used to undermine true beliefs. Will you commit to investigating before judging, especially about those who uphold the sunnah?
?
When you read about al-Ash'ari being attacked for affirming divine decree and God's attributes, do you feel the weight of defending these truths in your own life? Are you willing to stand firm on them even if it invites criticism from others around you?
?
Ibn Asakir warns that enemies strive to nullify the religion. Are there any practices or ideologies in your own environment that subtly oppose the sunnah—perhaps by denying God's complete control over all events or by downplaying His attributes? Will you actively identify and reject them?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir

The Fitna in Nishapur and Ibn Asakir's Exhortation
Ibn Asakir narrates the fitna and urges Muslims to actively defend al-Ash'ari and the truth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical fitna in Nishapur and Ibn Asakir's call for Muslims to defend the truth.

Core Idea
The fitna was a trial; Ibn Asakir urges each Muslim to defend the truth with supplication and concern.

Ibn Asakir describes the outbreak of the fitna in Nishapur and its widespread impact. He acknowledges that even well-meaning Muslims might doubt al-Ash'ari due to the controversy. He then explains his purpose in writing: to give every Sunni a share in defending the religion through sincere effort and prayer.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text and the translation. Notice the emotional tone and the direct address to the reader.
The phrase 'من يسمع يخل' is a proverb meaning 'whoever hears thinks'—i.e., hearsay can lead to wrong assumptions.
2
Understand the context of the fitna
The fitna began in Nishapur and spread. It caused great distress among Ahl al-Sunnah. Ibn Asakir is writing to clarify the situation.
Nishapur was a major center of learning and conflict between Ash'aris and Hanbalis.
3
Identify Ibn Asakir's purpose
He states he has written to allow every Sunni to have a share in defending the religion, through sincere supplication and care.
This shows his aim is unity and action, not mere polemics.
4
Reflect on the reward mentioned
He says that feeling pain for the truth merits a reward from Allah. Why is that significant?
It encourages emotional investment in defending orthodox beliefs.

حكاية ولا وصف، بل كل ذلك تصوير بتزوير وبهتان بغیر تقدیر. وما نقموا من الأشعرى إلا أنه قال بإثبات القدر الله خيره وشره نفعه وضره، وإثبات صفات الجلال الله من قدرته وعلمه وإرادته وحياته وبقائه وسمعه وبصره وكلامه ووجهه ويده وأن القرآن كلام الله غير مخلوق وأنه تعالى موجود تجوز رؤيته وأن إرادته نافذة فى مراداته وما لا يخفى من مسائل الأصول التي تخالف طرقه طرق المعتزلة والمجسمة فيها .. معاشر المسلمين الغياث الغياث سعوا في ابطال الدين وراموا هدم قواعد المسلمين وهيهات هيهات ( يريدون ليطفئوا نور الله بأفواههم ويأبى الله إلا أن يتم نوره ) وقد وعد الله للحق نصره وظهوره وللباطل محقه وثبوره إلا أن كتب الأشعرى في الآفاق مبثوثة ومذاهبه عند أهل السنة من الفريقين معروفة ومشهورة فمن وصفه بالبدعة علم أنه غير محق في دعواه وجميع أهل السنة خصمه فيما افتراه - ثم ذكر أربع مسائل شنع بها عليه وبين براءة ساحته فيما نسب منها إليه ثم قال - ولما ظهر ابتداء هذه الفتنة بنيسابور وانتشر في الأفاق خبره وعظم على قلوب كافة المسلمين من أهل السنة والجماعة أمره، ولم يبعد أن يخامر قلوب بعض أهل السلامة والوداعة توهم في بعض هذه المسائل ان لعل الامام أبا الحسن على بن اسمعيل الأشعري رحمه الله قال ببعض هذه المقالات في بعض كتبه ولقد قيل ( من يسمع يخل أثبتنا هذه التصول في شرح هذه الحالة وأوضحنا صورة الأمر بذكر هذه الجملة ليضرب كل من أهل السنة إذا وقف عليها بسهمه في الانتصار لدين الله من دعاء يخلصه واهتمام يصدقه وكل عن قلوبنا بالاستماع إلى هذه القصة يحمله، بل ثواب من الله على التوجع بذلك يستوجبه، والله غالب على أمره وله الحمد على ما يمضيه من أحكامه ويبرمه ويقضيه من افعاله فيما يؤخره ويقدمه، وصلواته على سيدنا المصطفى وعلى آله وسلم ولا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله العلى العظيم .

Rather, he deserves a reward from Allah for feeling pain about that. And Allah is dominant over His affair, and praise be to Him for the judgments He enacts and completes and the actions He decrees in what He delays and advances. And His blessings be upon our Master the Chosen one and upon his family and peace. And there is no power nor strength except with Allah, the Most High, the Magnificent.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a defense of al-Ash'ari by Ibn Asakir. It begins by stating that the criticisms of al-Ash'ari are baseless fabrications. It then lists the core beliefs of al-Ash'ari that provoked opposition: affirming divine decree (qadar) with its good and evil, affirming God's attributes (power, knowledge, will, life, permanence, hearing, sight, speech, face, and hands), the uncreatedness of the Quran, the possibility of seeing God in the afterlife, and the effectiveness of God's will. These principles, Ibn Asakir notes, conflict with the methods of the Mu'tazila and the Mujassima. He then cries out to the Muslim community for help, accusing the enemies of trying to destroy religion, and quotes the Quranic verse (9:32) about those who seek to extinguish Allah's light. He asserts that Allah has promised victory to truth and destruction to falsehood. Despite the attacks, al-Ash'ari's books are widespread and his school is well-known among both groups of Ahl al-Sunnah (likely the Ash'aris and Maturidis, or the Hanbalis and Ash'aris). Whoever calls him an innovator is false, and all Ahl al-Sunnah oppose that accuser. Ibn Asakir then mentions that he has listed four specific issues used to vilify al-Ash'ari and has shown his innocence. He describes the beginning of the fitna in Nishapur, its spread, and its effect on the hearts of Muslims. He explains that he wrote this clarification to allow every Muslim to participate in defending the religion, hoping for reward from Allah. The passage concludes with praise and blessings.

Key Terms
الفتنة
نيسابور
أهل السنة والجماعة

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Asakir, why did he write this clarification?
A) To attack the critics of al-Ash'ari
B) To allow every Sunni to participate in defending the religion through supplication and concern
C) To prove that al-Ash'ari was wrong
D) To show that the fitna was unimportant

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir wrote to equip every Sunni with a way to defend the truth—through heartfelt prayer and sincere care, which carries divine reward.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear someone slandering a scholar of the Sunnah, do you feel genuine pain in your heart? Ibn Asakir says that pain itself earns reward. If you feel indifference, what does that reveal about your love for the truth? Will you commit today to making even a small du'a for those who defend orthodoxy?
?
Ibn Asakir calls every Sunni to take a share in defending the religion through sincere supplication and truthful concern. When was the last time you actually made du'a for scholars who are unjustly attacked? Is your concern real, or just lip service? Will you set a daily reminder to include such du'a in your prayers?
?
The fitna distressed the hearts of Ahl al-Sunnah. Does the current state of division and slander in the Ummah affect you to the point of action? If not, what are you protecting in your heart that prevents that pain? Ask Allah to soften your heart and grant you sincere concern for His religion.

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
5 min
Scholarly Consensus on al-Ash'ari's Orthodoxy
A historical document from al-Qushayri and others affirming al-Ash'ari's status as an Imam of Ahl al-Hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that a documented consensus of prominent 5th-century hadith scholars and Sufis explicitly affirmed Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari as an Imam of Ahl al-Hadith and defended his school as that of Ahl al-Sunnah.

Core Idea
A collective testimony from major scholars defends al-Ash'ari as an Imam of Ahl al-Hadith.

This lesson presents a remarkable historical document preserved by Ibn Asakir. It is a written testimony (dhikr) from the renowned Sufi scholar Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri, signed by many other leading scholars of the 5th century AH. Their collective witness declares that al-Ash'ari was not a deviant but an Imam of the hadith scholars, and that attacking him is tantamount to attacking all Ahl al-Sunnah. By studying this document, you will see how the early Ash'ari school was rooted in Sunni orthodoxy.

Guided Path
1
Read the document's opening statement
Start by reading the passage from the beginning up to the first signature. Notice the strong language: 'The hadith scholars agreed that Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari was an Imam from the Imams of the hadith scholars.' This is the core claim.
The basmala is repeated three times, perhaps for emphasis.
2
Identify the accusation and defense
The document states that al-Ash'ari was a 'drawn sword' against the Mu'tazila, Rafida, and innovators. It then declares that any attack on him is an attack on all Ahl al-Sunnah. Ask yourself: why would such a strong defense be needed?
This shows the document was a response to critics who questioned al-Ash'ari's orthodoxy.
3
Observe the list of signatories
The passage lists many names, each confirming the statement. Notice the variety: hadith scholars, Sufis, jurists. This demonstrates broad agreement across different circles.
Some names are familiar, like al-Juwayni and al-Qushayri himself.
4
Reflect on the historical significance
Consider that this document is dated 436 AH, only about a century after al-Ash'ari's death. It shows that within the Ash'ari school's early period, its leading figures were publicly defending his legacy as a Sunni imam.

قال الامام الحافظ أبو القسم على بن اسمعيل بن الحسن رضى دفع إلى أبو محمد عبد الواحد بن عبد الماجد بن عبد الواحد بن عبد الكريم بن هوازن القشيري الصوفي النيسابوری بدمشق مكتوبا بخط جده الامام أبى القسم القشيري، وأنا اعرف الخط فوجدت فيه : بسم الله الله الله الرحمن الرحيم اتفق أصحاب الحديث ان أبا الحسن على بن اسمعيل الأشعرى رضى عنه كان إماما من أئمة أصحاب الحديث . ومذهبه مذهب أصحاب الحديث تكلم في أصول الديانات على طريقة أهل السنة ورد على المخالفين من أهل الزيغ والبدعة، وكان على المعتزلة والروافض والمبتدعين من أهل القبلة والخارجين من الملة سيفا مسلولا، ومن طعن فيه أو قدح أو لغنه أو سبه فقد بسط لسان السوء في جميع أهل السنة بذلنا . خطوطنا طائعين بذلك فى هذا الذكر فى ذى القعدة سنة ست وثلاثين وأربعمائة والأمر على هذه الجملة المذكورة في هذا الذكر وكتبه عبدالكريم ابن هوازن القشيري، وفيه بخط أبي عبدالله الخبازى المقرى كذلك يعرفه محمد بن على الخبازى وهذا خطه وبخط الامام أبى محمد الجويني الأمر على هذه الجملة المذكورة فيه، وكتبه عبدالله بن يوسف وبخط أبي الفتح . الشاشى الأمر على هذه الجملة التي ذكرت وكتبه نصر بن محمد الشاشي بخطه وبخط آخر الأمر على هذه الجملة المذكورة فيه وكتبه على بن أحمد الجويني بخطه وبخط أبى الفتح العمرى الهروى الفقيه الأمر على هذه الجملة المذكورة فيه وكتبه ناصر بن الحسين بخطه وبخط الأيوبي الأمر على الجملة التي ذكرت فيه وكتبه أحمد بن محمد بن الحسن بن أبي أيوب بخطه وبخط أخيه الأمر على هذه الجملة المذكورة فيه وكتبه على بن محمد بن أبي أيوب بخطه وبخط الأمام أبي عثمان الصابوني الأمر على الجملة المذكورة وكتبه اسماعيل بن عبدالرحمن الصابوني وبخط ابنه أبى الصابوني، الأمر على الجملة المذكورة صدر هذا الذكر وكتبه عبد الله ابن اسماعيل الصابوني وبخط الشريف البكرى الأمر على نحو مابين درج هذا الذكر، وكتبه على بن الحسن البكرى الزبيرى بخطه وبخط آخر هو إمام من أئمة أصحاب الحديث والأمر على ما وصف في هذا الذكر وكتبه محمد بن الحسن بيده وبخط أبى الحسن الملقاباذى أبو الحسن الأشعرى رحمة الله عليه امام من أئمة اصحاب الحديث ورئيس من رؤسائهم في أصول الدين وطريقته طريقة السنة والجماعة ودينه واعتقاده مرضی مقبول عند الفريقين وكتبه على بن محمد الملقاباذى بخطه وبخط عبد الجبار الاسفراينى بالفارسية : این بو الحسن الأشعرى امام است که خداوند عز نصر
Al-Imam al-Hafiz Abu al-Qasim Ali ibn Isma'il ibn al-Hasan (may Allah be pleased with him) said: Abu Muhammad Abd al-Wahid ibn Abd al-Majid ibn Abd al-Wahid ibn Abd al-Karim ibn Hawazin al-Qushayri al-Sufi al-Naysaburi gave to me in Damascus a written document in the handwriting of his grandfather al-Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri, and I recognized the handwriting. I found in it: In the name of Allah, Allah, Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. The hadith scholars (as-hab al-hadith) agreed that Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Isma'il al-Ash'ari (may Allah be pleased with him) was an Imam from the Imams of the hadith scholars. His school is the school of the hadith scholars. He spoke on the principles of religions according to the way of Ahl al-Sunnah and refuted the opponents from the people of deviation and innovation. And he was against the Mu'tazila, the Rafida, and the innovators from the people of the qibla and those who left the milla, a drawn sword. And whoever attacks him or slanders him or curses him or insults him has extended the tongue of evil against all Ahl al-Sunnah. We offered our signatures willingly to that in this dhikr in Dhu al-Qi'dah of the year 436 (AH). And the matter is upon what is mentioned in this dhikr. Written by Abd al-Karim ibn Hawazin al-Qushayri. And in it, in the handwriting of Abu Abd Allah al-Khabbazi al-Muqri, similarly, Muhammad ibn Ali al-Khabbazi knows him, and this is his handwriting. And in the handwriting of al-Imam Abu Muhammad al-Juwayni: the matter is upon what is mentioned in it. Written by Abd Allah ibn Yusuf. And in the handwriting of Abu al-Fath al-Shashi: the matter is upon what is mentioned. Written by Nasr ibn Muhammad al-Shashi in his handwriting. And in another handwriting: the matter is upon what is mentioned in it. Written by Ali ibn Ahmad al-Juwayni in his handwriting. And in the handwriting of Abu al-Fath al-Umari al-Harawi al-Faqih: the matter is upon what is mentioned in it. Written by Nasir ibn al-Husayn in his handwriting. And in the handwriting of al-Ayyubi: the matter is upon the statement mentioned in it. Written by Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Abi Ayyub in his handwriting. And in the handwriting of his brother: the matter is upon what is mentioned in it. Written by Ali ibn Muhammad ibn Abi Ayyub in his handwriting. And in the handwriting of al-Imam Abu Uthman al-Sabuni: the matter is upon the mentioned statement. Written by Isma'il ibn Abd al-Rahman al-Sabuni. And in the handwriting of his son Abu al-Sabuni: the matter is upon the mentioned statement, which is the opening of this dhikr. Written by Abd Allah ibn Isma'il al-Sabuni. And in the handwriting of al-Sharif al-Bakri: the matter is upon what is between the folds of this dhikr. Written by Ali ibn al-Hasan al-Bakri al-Zubayri in his handwriting. And in another handwriting: He is an Imam from the Imams of the hadith scholars, and the matter is upon what is described in this dhikr. Written by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan with his hand. And in the handwriting of Abu al-Hasan al-Malqabadi: Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari (may Allah have mercy on him) is an Imam from the Imams of the hadith scholars and a chief from their chiefs in the principles of religion, and his way is the way of the Sunnah and the Community, and his religion and belief are accepted and approved by both groups. Written by Ali ibn Muhammad al-Malqabadi in his handwriting. And in the handwriting of Abd al-Jabbar al-Isfarayini in Persian: 'In Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari imam ast ki Khudawand 'azza...' (This Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari is an Imam that God, might and majesty...)
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage presents a historical document (dhikr) that Ibn Asakir received from Abu Muhammad al-Qushayri, written in the hand of his grandfather, the famous Sufi and scholar Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri. The document begins by stating that the hadith scholars (as-hab al-hadith) unanimously agree that Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari was an Imam of the hadith scholars, his school is that of the hadith scholars, he spoke on the principles of religion according to the way of Ahl al-Sunnah, and he refuted deviants. It declares that he was a drawn sword against the Mu'tazila, Rafida, and other innovators, and that any attack on him is an attack on all Ahl al-Sunnah. The document is dated Dhu al-Qi'dah 436 AH. Then follows a list of signatories, each confirming the statement: Abd al-Karim ibn Hawazin al-Qushayri (the original writer), Abu Abd Allah al-Khabbazi al-Muqri, Muhammad ibn Ali al-Khabbazi, Abu Muhammad al-Juwayni, Abd Allah ibn Yusuf, Abu al-Fath al-Shashi (Nasr ibn Muhammad), Ali ibn Ahmad al-Juwayni, Abu al-Fath al-Umari al-Harawi (Nasir ibn al-Husayn), al-Ayyubi (Ahmad and his brother Ali), Abu Uthman al-Sabuni (Isma'il and his son Abd Allah), al-Sharif al-Bakri (Ali ibn al-Hasan), an unnamed signatory (Muhammad ibn al-Hasan), Abu al-Hasan al-Malqabadi (Ali ibn Muhammad), and Abd al-Jabbar al-Isfarayini, who added a Persian translation. The document ends abruptly. This passage serves as strong external testimony to al-Ash'ari's orthodoxy from multiple prominent scholars of the 5th century AH.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That only one or two scholars supported al-Ash'ari; this document shows a consensus of many prominent hadith scholars and Sufis.
Correction: This document records the explicit agreement of numerous leading scholars, including al-Qushayri, al-Juwayni, al-Sabuni, and others, all affirming al-Ash'ari's orthodoxy and his place as an Imam of Ahl al-Hadith.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you have ever dismissed or criticized the Ash'ari school based on hearsay, what does this document—signed by so many respected scholars of Ahl al-Hadith—demand of you now? Will you seek the truth humbly or persist in ignoring clear evidence?
?
The document warns that attacking al-Ash'ari is attacking all Ahl al-Sunnah. Have you ever spoken ill of a scholar without verifying their stance? What concrete step will you take today to repent from that and to defend the honor of scholars you disagree with?
?
These scholars willingly put their signatures to a public testimony. If you were asked to publicly defend a scholar you believe is right, would you have the courage to do so? What holds you back from standing firm for the truth as you know it?

Consensus of Ahl al-Hadith on Al-Ash'ari's Orthodoxy
Ibn Asakir records the collective testimony of many scholars affirming al-Ash'ari's Imamate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Ahl al-Hadith collectively affirmed Imam al-Ash'ari as one of their own, and the historical documentation of this consensus.

Core Idea
The consensus of Ahl al-Hadith confirms al-Ash'ari's orthodoxy.

This passage from Ibn 'Asakir's Tabyin Kidhb al-Muftari presents a remarkable historical document: a written consensus from leading scholars of Ahl al-Hadith affirming that Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari was an Imam from among them. It serves as a direct refutation of later claims that al-Ash'ari departed from the path of the Salaf.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening declaration
Notice the phrase 'اتفق أصحاب الحديث' (The people of hadith agreed) and understand its weight as a statement of collective consensus.
2
Identify the groups al-Ash'ari refuted
The passage mentions Mu'tazila, Rawafid, and innovators. Note how al-Ash'ari is portrayed as a defender of Ahl al-Sunnah.
3
Reflect on the warning
Read the warning that attacking al-Ash'ari is equivalent to attacking all Ahl al-Sunnah. Ask yourself why this is significant.
4
Survey the signatories
Scan the list of scholars who attested. Notice the repetition of the phrase 'الأمر على هذه الجملة' and the variety of authorities.
The unanimity reinforces the consensus.

اتفق أصحاب الحديث ان أبا الحسن على بن اسمعيل الأشعرى رضى عنه كان إماما من أئمة أصحاب الحديث . ومذهبه مذهب أصحاب الحديث تكلم في أصول الديانات على طريقة أهل السنة ورد على المخالفين من أهل الزيغ والبدعة، وكان على المعتزلة والروافض والمبتدعين من أهل القبلة والخارجين من الملة سيفا مسلولا، ومن طعن فيه أو قدح أو لغنه أو سبه فقد بسط لسان السوء في جميع أهل السنة بذلنا خطوطنا طائعين بذلك فى هذا الذكر فى ذى القعدة سنة ست وثلاثين وأربعمائة والأمر على هذه الجملة المذكورة في هذا الذكر وكتبه عبدالكريم ابن هوازن القشيري، وفيه بخط أبي عبدالله الخبازى المقرى كذلك يعرفه محمد بن على الخبازى وهذا خطه وبخط الامام أبى محمد الجويني الأمر على هذه الجملة المذكورة فيه، وكتبه عبدالله بن يوسف وبخط أبي الفتح الشاشى الأمر على هذه الجملة التي ذكرت وكتبه نصر بن محمد الشاشي بخطه وبخط آخر الأمر على هذه الجملة المذكورة فيه وكتبه على بن أحمد الجويني بخطه وبخط أبى الفتح العمرى الهروى الفقيه الأمر على هذه الجملة المذكورة فيه وكتبه ناصر بن الحسين بخطه وبخط الأيوبي الأمر على الجملة التي ذكرت فيه وكتبه أحمد بن محمد بن الحسن بن أبي أيوب بخطه وبخط أخيه الأمر على هذه الجملة المذكورة فيه وكتبه على بن محمد بن أبي أيوب بخطه وبخط الأمام أبي عثمان الصابوني الأمر على الجملة المذكورة وكتبه اسماعيل بن عبدالرحمن الصابوني وبخط ابنه أبى الصابوني، الأمر على الجملة المذكورة صدر هذا الذكر وكتبه عبد الله ابن اسماعيل الصابوني وبخط الشريف البكرى الأمر على نحو مابين درج هذا الذكر، وكتبه على بن الحسن البكرى الزبيرى بخطه وبخط آخر هو إمام من أئمة أصحاب الحديث والأمر على ما وصف في هذا الذكر وكتبه محمد بن الحسن بيده وبخط أبى الحسن الملقاباذى أبو الحسن الأشعرى رحمة الله عليه امام من أئمة اصحاب الحديث ورئيس من رؤسائهم في أصول الدين وطريقته طريقة السنة والجماعة ودينه واعتقاده مرضی مقبول عند الفريقين وكتبه على بن محمد الملقاباذى بخطه
The people of hadith (Ahl al-Hadith) agreed that Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Isma'il al-Ash'ari (may Allah be pleased with him) was an Imam from among the Imams of the people of hadith. His madhhab is the madhhab of the people of hadith; he spoke on the foundations of religions according to the way of Ahl al-Sunnah and refuted those who opposed from among the people of deviation and innovation. He was against the Mu'tazila, the Rawafid, and the innovators from among the people of the Qibla and those who left the religion, a drawn sword. Whoever attacks him, disparages him, curses him, or insults him has indeed extended the tongue of evil against all Ahl al-Sunnah. We have written our signatures willingly in this record in Dhu al-Qa'dah in the year 436 AH. The matter is as mentioned in this record. Written by 'Abd al-Karim ibn Hawazin al-Qushayri. And in it in the handwriting of Abu 'Abd Allah al-Khabbazi al-Muqri; similarly, Muhammad ibn 'Ali al-Khabbazi recognizes it, and this is his handwriting. And in the handwriting of Imam Abu Muhammad al-Juwayni: the matter is as mentioned in it. Written by 'Abd Allah ibn Yusuf. And in the handwriting of Abu al-Fath al-Shashi: the matter is as mentioned. Written by Nasr ibn Muhammad al-Shashi in his own hand. And in another handwriting: the matter is as mentioned in it. Written by 'Ali ibn Ahmad al-Juwayni in his own hand. And in the handwriting of Abu al-Fath al-'Umari al-Hirawi al-Faqih: the matter is as mentioned in it. Written by Nasir ibn al-Husayn in his own hand. And in the handwriting of al-Ayyubi: the matter is as mentioned in it. Written by Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Abi Ayyub in his own hand. And in the handwriting of his brother: the matter is as mentioned in it. Written by 'Ali ibn Muhammad ibn Abi Ayyub in his own hand. And in the handwriting of Imam Abu 'Uthman al-Sabuni: the matter is as mentioned. Written by Isma'il ibn 'Abd al-Rahman al-Sabuni. And in the handwriting of his son, Abu al-Sabuni: the matter is as mentioned at the beginning of this record. Written by 'Abd Allah ibn Isma'il al-Sabuni. And in the handwriting of al-Sharif al-Bakri: the matter is similar to what is recorded in this record. Written by 'Ali ibn al-Hasan al-Bakri al-Zubayri in his own hand. And in another handwriting: he is an Imam from the Imams of the people of hadith, and the matter is as described in this record. Written by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan with his own hand. And in the handwriting of Abu al-Hasan al-Malqabadi: Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari (may Allah have mercy on him) is an Imam from the Imams of the people of hadith and a chief from among their chiefs in the fundamentals of religion; his way is the way of the Sunnah and the community; his religion and creed are sound and accepted by both groups. Written by 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Malqabadi in his own hand.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is a declaration of consensus from multiple prominent scholars of Ahl al-Hadith affirming that Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari is one of their Imams. It begins with a straightforward statement of agreement: 'The people of hadith agreed that Abu al-Hasan…was an Imam from among the Imams of the people of hadith.' It then defines his madhhab as the madhhab of Ahl al-Hadith, emphasizing his role in defending the foundations of religion according to the method of Ahl al-Sunnah and refuting deviant groups such as the Mu'tazila and Rawafid. The text warns that anyone who attacks al-Ash'ari has attacked all Ahl al-Sunnah. Following this, a list of signatories and their statements is provided, each attesting to the correctness of the claim. The list includes well-known figures like al-Qushayri, al-Juwayni, al-Sabuni, and others, each writing in their own hand or attesting to the handwriting. The recurring phrase 'the matter is as mentioned in this record' emphasizes their unanimous agreement. The final signature from al-Malqabadi explicitly states that al-Ash'ari is an Imam and chief in the fundamentals of religion, his way is that of the Sunnah and Jama'ah, and his creed is accepted by both groups (likely Ash'aris and others). The passage serves as a historical document refuting later claims that al-Ash'ari was not part of Ahl al-Hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari was a leader of the Mu'tazila or innovator.
Correction: This passage shows that Ahl al-Hadith themselves considered him an Imam and their madhhab, directly refuting the claim.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the collective testimony recorded in this passage?
A) Al-Ash'ari was a leader of the Mu'tazila.

Persian Witness to al-Ash'ari's Virtue
A Persian testimony linking al-Ash'ari to a Qur'anic verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a Persian testimony connects Imam al-Ash'ari to a Qur'anic verse through his grandfather Abu Musa al-Ash'ari.

Core Idea
A Persian witness links al-Ash'ari to divine love via his grandfather.

This passage presents a remarkable piece of historical testimony. A Persian scholar writes that Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari is the Imam referred to in the verse 'Soon Allah will bring a people whom He loves and who love Him,' and that the Prophet himself pointed to al-Ash'ari's grandfather, Abu Musa, when the verse was revealed. Let's examine this claim and its transmission.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English carefully to understand the claim being made. Notice the Persian phrase and the subsequent Arabic interpretation.
The passage includes both the original Persian and its Arabic gloss.
2
Identify the key figures
Identify Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, and the transmitter 'Abd al-Jabbar al-Isfara'ini. Also note the role of Ibn 'Asakir as the compiler.
Abu Musa is the grandfather of al-Ash'ari.
3
Understand the claim
The testimony claims that the verse 'Soon Allah will bring a people...' was revealed about al-Ash'ari's lineage, and that the Prophet pointed to Abu Musa, indicating that al-Ash'ari's people (the Ash'aris) are the ones meant.
This elevates al-Ash'ari's theological position.
4
Analyze the transmission
Note how Ibn 'Asakir copied the lines from a scroll and provides his own interpretation. This shows careful transmission of historical evidence.
Ibn 'Asakir is known for his meticulous documentation.
5
Reflect on the misunderstanding
Understand that the verse was not revealed about al-Ash'ari directly but about his grandfather's people. The testimony is about lineage, not direct revelation.
This clarifies a common misinterpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبخط عبد الجبار الاسفراينى بالفارسية : این بو الحسن الأشعرى امام است که خداوند عز وجل این آیت درشان وی فرستاد ( فسوف يأتى الله بقوم يحبهم ويحبونه ) ومصطفى علیه السلام در آن وقت بجد وی اشارت کردبو موسى اشعرى فقال ( هم قوم (هذا وكتبه عبد الجبار بن علی بن محمد الاسفرايني بخطه وبخط ابنه هكذا يقول محمد بن عبد الجبار بن محمد . قال الامام الحافظ الله رضی عنه نقلت هذه الخطوط على نصها من ذلك الدرج ونقلها غيرى من الفقهاء وتفسير قول هذا الفارسي : هذا أبو الحسن كان إماما ولما أنزل عز وجل قوله ( فسوف يأتى الله بقوم يحبهم ويحبونه ) أشار المصطفى صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى أبي موسى رضى الله عنه وقال هم قوم هذا
And in the handwriting of 'Abd al-Jabbar al-Isfara'ini in Persian: 'This Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari is an Imam concerning whom Allah, Mighty and Majestic, sent down this verse: “Soon Allah will bring a people whom He loves and who love Him.” And the Chosen One (peace be upon him) at that time pointed to his grandfather Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and said: “They are the people of this.”' Written by 'Abd al-Jabbar ibn 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Isfara'ini in his own hand. When Allah, Mighty and Majestic, revealed His saying: “Soon Allah will bring a people whom He loves and who love Him,” the Chosen One (peace be upon him) pointed to Abu Musa (may Allah be pleased with him) and said: “They are the people of this.”'

Commentary
This passage presents a Persian testimony from 'Abd al-Jabbar al-Isfara'ini, written in Persian, claiming that Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari is the Imam referred to in the Qur'anic verse from Surat al-Ma'idah (5:54): 'Soon Allah will bring a people whom He loves and who love Him.' The Persian text states that the Prophet (peace be upon him) pointed to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari (al-Ash'ari's grandfather) and said 'They are the people of this' when the verse was revealed. After the Persian quote, the author (Ibn 'Asakir) explains that he copied these lines from the original scroll and that other jurists also copied them. He then provides an Arabic interpretation of the Persian statement, clarifying that the claim is that al-Ash'ari is an Imam and that the verse and prophetic pointing refer to his lineage. The passage serves as a witness to the high status of al-Ash'ari, connecting him directly to a divine commendation and prophetic praise.

Another Narration: Al-Ash'ari and the Verse of Love
Ibn Asakir cites a book relating the verse to al-Ash'ari's lineage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how this second narration reinforces the connection between Imam al-Ash'ari and the prophetic praise through his lineage.

Core Idea
Prophetic approval through lineage confirms al-Ash'ari's exemplary status.

In this short passage, Ibn Asakir presents another chain of transmission that explicitly ties Imam al-Ash'ari to a verse of divine love. The narration claims that when the verse 'Soon Allah will bring a people whom He loves and who love Him' was revealed, the Prophet pointed to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, the grandfather of the Imam, indicating that his descendants would embody those qualities. This provides a second source for the high status of al-Ash'ari.

قال الامام الحافظ رضى الله عنه : قرأت فى كتاب أبي يعقوب يوسف ابن علی بن محمد المؤدب الذي قرأه على أبى الفتوح بن عباس عن عبيد (۱) بل تفسيره : أبو الحسن الأشعرى هذا امام انزل الله عزل وجل في شأنه هذه الآية ( فسوف يأتى الله بقوم يحبهم ويحبونه وأشار النبى صلى الله عليه وسلم لما نزلت إلى جده أبي موسى الأشعرى وقال ( هم قوم هذا )

Commentary
This short passage is another narration cited by Ibn 'Asakir to support the connection between al-Ash'ari and the verse from Surat al-Ma'idah. This interpretation reaffirms the earlier Persian testimony, providing a second source for the claim. The phrase 'rather, its interpretation' (بل تفسيره) suggests this is the correct or more precise interpretation of the earlier statement or of the verse's application. The passage highlights the importance of lineage and prophetic approval in establishing al-Ash'ari's authority.

The Prophetic Testimony for Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari
Ibn Asakir cites two narrations linking a Quranic verse to al-Ash'ari.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how two narrations interpret Quran 5:54 as referring to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and his lineage.

Core Idea
The Quranic verse 'Soon Allah will bring a people' points to al-Ash'ari through his grandfather.

Imam Ibn Asakir presents two independent traditions that connect the Quranic verse 5:54 directly to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. These narrations serve to counter accusations against the Ash'ari school by grounding its founder in scriptural and prophetic authority. The passage shows how later scholars used hadith to legitimize theological figures.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully. Notice that it contains two distinct narrations separated by a repetition of the phrase 'قال الامام الحافظ رضی عنه'.
The first narration is from a scroll, the second from a book.
2
Identify the two narrations
In your own words, summarize what each narration says about the verse and Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.
Pay attention to the chain of transmission for each.
3
Understand the link to Abu Musa
Why does the Prophet point to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari? How does that connect to Abu al-Hasan?
Abu Musa is the grandfather of Abu al-Hasan.
4
Reflect on the purpose
What is the author trying to prove by including these narrations? Consider the sectarian context.
This legitimizes al-Ash'ari as a divinely favored imam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الامام الحافظ رضی عنه نقلت هذه الخطوط على نصها من ذلك الدرج ونقلها غيرى من الفقهاء وتفسير قول هذا الفارسي : هذا أبو الحسن كان إماما ولما أنزل عز وجل قوله ( فسوف يأتى الله بقوم يحبهم ويحبونه ) أشار المصطفى صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى أبي موسى رضى الله عنه وقال هم قوم هذا. قال الامام الحافظ رضى الله عنه : قرأت فى كتاب أبي يعقوب يوسف ابن علی بن محمد المؤدب الذي قرأه على أبى الفتوح بن عباس عن عبيد بل تفسيره : أبو الحسن الأشعرى هذا امام انزل الله عزل وجل في شأنه هذه الآية ( فسوف يأتى الله بقوم يحبهم ويحبونه ) وأشار النبى صلى الله عليه وسلم لما نزلت إلى جده أبي موسى الأشعرى وقال ( هم قوم هذا ).
Imam al-Hafiz, may Allah be pleased with him, said: I copied these lines exactly as they were from that scroll, and others among the jurists copied them. The interpretation of the Persian's statement: This Abu al-Hasan was an imam. When Allah, Mighty and Majestic, revealed His words 'Soon Allah will bring a people whom He loves and who love Him,' the Chosen One, peace be upon him, pointed to Abu Musa, may Allah be pleased with him, and said, 'They are this people's people.' Imam al-Hafiz, may Allah be pleased with him, said: I read in the book of Abu Ya'qub Yusuf ibn Ali ibn Muhammad al-Mu'addib, which he read to Abu al-Futuh ibn Abbas from Ubayd, the interpretation: Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari is this imam. Allah, Mighty and Majestic, revealed this verse concerning him: 'Soon Allah will bring a people whom He loves and who love Him,' and the Prophet, peace be upon him, when it was revealed, pointed to his grandfather Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and said, 'They are this people's people.'
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage presents two independent chains of narration that interpret the Quranic verse 5:54 as referring to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari (d. 324/935), the founder of the Ash'ari school of theology. The first narration comes from Imam al-Hafiz (likely Ibn 'Asakir himself), who transmits from a scroll written by 'Abd al-Jabbar al-Isfarayini and others, including a Persian gloss identifying 'this Abu al-Hasan' as an imam, and stating that when the verse was revealed, the Prophet Muhammad pointed to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari (the grandfather of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari) and said 'They are this people's people' — meaning the descendants of Abu Musa. The second narration is from the book of Abu Ya'qub al-Mu'addib, who transmits via two intermediaries that the verse was revealed concerning Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari himself, and that the Prophet pointed to his grandfather Abu Musa. Both narrations serve to legitimize al-Ash'ari as a divinely favored figure, using scriptural and prophetic testimony to counter his detractors.

Key Terms
أبو الحسن الأشعري
فسوف يأتي الله بقوم
أبو موسى الأشعري
إمام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Quran 5:54 refers to the companions in general and not specifically to the lineage of al-Ash'ari.
Correction: The narrations explicitly state that the verse was revealed concerning Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, with the Prophet pointing to his grandfather Abu Musa as the progenitor of the people mentioned.

A) Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari
B) Abu Musa al-Ash'ari
C) The Persians
D) The Mu'tazila

Key Takeaway
Two independent narrations link Quran 5:54 to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, using prophetic testimony to legitimize his status as an imam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Al-Juwayni's Defense of al-Ash'ari from False Accusations
Al-Juwayni defends al-Ash'ari from false accusations on ijtihad and other issues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the false accusations made against al-Ash'ari and how al-Juwayni refuted them based on al-Ash'ari's own writings.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's own books prove the slanders against him false.

In this passage, the great Ash'ari theologian Imam al-Juwayni writes a spirited defense of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari against a series of accusations made by innovators. After clarifying al-Ash'ari's position on ijtihad—where he held that all mujtahids are correct in subsidiary matters—al-Juwayni lists several false attributions and declares that he has examined al-Ash'ari's works and found them to be the opposite of what his detractors claim. This lesson will help you see how early Ash'ari scholars defended their founder's legacy from distortion.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Juwayni's opening on ijtihad
Notice how al-Juwayni distinguishes between principles (usul) and branches (furu') regarding who is correct among the mujtahids. This sets the stage for al-Ash'ari's view.
Al-Ash'ari held that all mujtahids are correct in branches, which differed from al-Shafi'i's own position.
2
Identify the list of false accusations
Al-Juwayni enumerates several claims made by the innovators against al-Ash'ari: denying the Qur'an in the mushaf, denying a prophet in his grave, exception in faith, negation of pre-eternal power, takfir of commoners, and obligating knowledge of proofs.
These are serious theological charges that could undermine al-Ash'ari's orthodoxy.
3
Understand al-Juwayni's refutation
Al-Juwayni states that he examined al-Ash'ari's books and found all these accusations to be false. He attributes the slanders to envy because al-Ash'ari exposed the errors of the innovators.
This shows the importance of returning to primary sources rather than relying on hearsay.
4
Reflect on the lesson's significance
Consider why it matters that al-Ash'ari's true positions are defended. This passage demonstrates the early Ash'ari commitment to textual verification and protects the founder from misrepresentation.
The same principle applies today: we must verify claims about scholars from their own works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر الشيخ الامام ركن الدين أبو محمد عبد الله بن يوسف الجويني رحمه الله في آخر كتاب صنفه وسماه عقيدة أصحاب الامام المطلبي الشافعي رضي الله عنه وكافة أهل السنة والجماعة وقال : ونعتقد ان المصيب من اجتهدين في الأصول والفروع واحد ويجب التعيين في الأصول فأما في الفروع فربما يتأتى التعيين وربما لايتأتى ومذهب الشيخ أبي الحسن رحمه تصويب المجتهدين في الفروع وليس ذلك مذهب الشافعي رضي الله عنه وأبو الحسن احد أصحاب الشافعى رضى الله عنهم، فإذا خالفه في شيء ا عرضنا عنه فيه ومن هذا القبيل قوله ان لاصيغة للأمر وتقل وتعز مخالفته أصول الشافعى رضى الله عنه، ونصوصه وربما نسب المبتدعون إليه أنه يقول ليس فى المصحف قرآن ولا في القبر نبي، وكذلك الاستثناء في الإيمان ونفى قدرة الخلق فى الأزل وتكفير العوام وايجاب علم الدليل عليهم وقد تصفحت ما تصفحت من كتبه وتأملت نصوصه في هذه المسائل فوجدتها كلها خلاف ما نسب إليه ولا عجب ان اعترضوا عليه واخترصوا فإنه رحمه فاضح القدرية وعامة المبتدعة وكاشف عوراتهم ولا خير فيمن لا يعرف حاسده.
And the Shaykh Imam Rukn al-Din Abu Muhammad Abdullah ibn Yusuf al-Juwayni, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned at the end of a book he authored, which he named 'The Creed of the Followers of Imam al-Muttalibi al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him, and all the People of the Sunnah and the Community,' and said: We believe that the one who is correct among those who exert independent judgment (mujtahidun) in principles (usul) and branches (furu') is one, and specification (ta'yin) is obligatory in principles. As for branches, specification may be attained and may not be attained. The school of Shaykh Abu al-Hasan, may Allah have mercy on him, is to declare all mujtahids correct in the branches, and that is not the school of al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him. Abu al-Hasan is one of the followers of al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with them. So if he contradicts him in something, we turn away from him in that. Among this is his statement that there is no verbal form (sigha) for the command, a view that is rare and mighty, and his contradiction of the principles and texts of al-Shafi'i. The innovators sometimes attribute to him that he says there is no Quran in the mushaf and no prophet in the grave, likewise exceptive statements (istithna') in faith, negation of the creatures' power in pre-eternity, declaring the common people disbelievers (takfir al-'awamm), and making knowledge of the proof obligatory upon them. And I have examined what I have examined of his books and contemplated his texts on these issues, and I found them all contrary to what is attributed to him. And it is no wonder that they opposed him and summarized, for he, may Allah have mercy on him, exposed the Qadariyya and all innovators and uncovered their weaknesses, and there is no good in one who does not know his envier.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a theological and historical defense of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari by Imam al-Juwayni (d. 478/1085), a leading Ash'ari theologian. Al-Juwayni writes in his book on creed, stating the Ash'ari position on ijtihad: in fundamental principles (usul al-din), only one mujtahid is correct and specification of the correct view is necessary, while in subsidiary legal rulings (furu'), multiple correct views are possible. He notes that al-Ash'ari held the view that all mujtahids are correct in branches, which differs from al-Shafi'i's own position. Al-Juwayni then addresses accusations made by innovators against al-Ash'ari: that he denied that the Quran is in the mushaf (i.e., the physical book), that he denied that a prophet is in his grave (i.e., bodily life), that he made exception in faith (i.e., saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills'), that he negated the creatures' capacity for action in pre-eternity, that he declared the common people disbelievers, and that he required knowledge of theological proofs for salvation. Al-Juwayni asserts that after examining al-Ash'ari's own writings, he found these accusations to be false. He attributes these accusations to the innovators' hatred, because al-Ash'ari exposed their errors and weaknesses.

Key Terms
المجتهدين
الأصول والفروع
التصويب
المبتدعون
الاستثناء في الإيمان
تكفير العوام
القدرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari denied that the Quran is in the physical mushaf and that the Prophet is alive in his grave.
Correction: Al-Juwayni states that after examining al-Ash'ari's own writings, he found these claims to be false. Al-Ash'ari's actual positions are contrary to these accusations.

Checkpoint
According to al-Juwayni, what did al-Ash'ari hold regarding the ijtihad of scholars in subsidiary legal rulings?
A) Only one mujtahid is correct
B) All mujtahids are correct
C) No ijtihad is permissible
D) Only the first four generations are correct

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's true theological positions can be verified from his own writings, which refute the slanders of his opponents.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What false claims have you accepted about a scholar or group without verifying from their own writings? How can you—starting today—commit to reading primary sources before forming judgments?
?
Al-Juwayni defended al-Ash'ari by examining his books. Is there a scholar you have misunderstood or criticized based on hearsay? Will you seek out their actual works to correct your understanding?
?
The innovators slandered al-Ash'ari out of envy because he exposed their errors. Whose errors are you afraid to confront because it might provoke hostility? How will you embody the courage of al-Juwayni in defending the truth?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
intermediate
5 min
The Mihna and the Early Sunni Mutakallimun
Ibn Asakir describes the Mihna and the early Sunni mutakallimun's response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the context of the Mihna and how early Sunni mutakallimun defended orthodoxy against the Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
The Mihna was a crucible that forged Sunni theology through patient refutation.

The early Abbasid era saw a state-imposed inquisition enforcing the Mu'tazilite doctrine of a created Quran. Sunni scholars faced immense pressure, yet a group of pious theologians quietly authored defenses of the faith. This passage from Ibn Asakir sets the stage for the emergence of a towering defender: Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mihna history
Read about the trial under al-Ma'mun and al-Mu'tasim, and how Ahmad ibn Hanbal's refusal to debate was used against the Sunnis.
The term 'Mihna' refers to the inquisition, a period of persecution.
2
Identify the early Sunni theologians
Notice the names of early mutakallimun who refuted the Mu'tazila without mixing with them: Abd al-Aziz al-Makki, al-Harith al-Muhasibi, Abdullah ibn Kullab.
These scholars combined asceticism with theological refutation.
3
Reflect on their strategy
Consider why they avoided direct contact with innovators yet wrote books against them. What does this say about their approach?
This sets the stage for al-Ash'ari's different approach later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نا أبو عبد الله محمد بن موسی بن عمار الكلاعى المايرقى الفقيه قال : أعظم ما كانت المحنة یعنی زمن المأمون والمعتصم، فتورع من مجادلتهم أحمد بن حنبل رضی الله عنه فمو هوا بذلك على الملوك وقالوا لهم انهم يعنون أهل السنة يفرون من المناظرة، لما يعلمونه من ضعفهم عن نصرة الباطل، وأنهم لا حجة بأيديهم وشتعوا بذلك عليهم حتى امتحن في زمانهم أحمد بن حنبل وغيره فأخذ الناس حينئذ بالقول بخلق القرآن، حتى ما كان تقبل شهادة شاهد ولا يستقضى قاض ولا يفتي مفت لا يقول بخلق القرآن، وكان في ذلك الوقت من المتكلمين جماعة كعبد العزيز المكي والحارث المحاسبي وعبدالله ابن كلاب وجماعة غيرهم، وكانوا أولى زهد وتقشف لم ير أحد منهم أن يطأ لأهل البدع بساطا ولا ان يداخلهم فكانوا يردون عليهم ويؤلفون الكتب في إدحاض حججهم، إلى ان نشأ بعدهم وعاصر بعضهم بالبصرة أيام اسماعيل القاضي ببغداد أبو الحسن على بن اسماعيل بن أبي بشر الأشعرى رضى الله عنه وصنف فى هذا العلم لأهل السنة التصانيف وألف لهم التواليف حتى أدحض حجج المعتزلة وكسر شوكتهم، وكان يقصدهم بنفسه يناظرهم فكلم فى ذلك وقيل له كيف تخالط أهل البدع وتقصدهم بنفسك، وقد أمرت بهجرهم فقال هم فقال هم أولو رياسة منهم الوالي والقاضي ولرياستهم لا ينزلون إلى فإذا كانوا هم لا ينزلون الى ولا أسير انا إليهم فكيف يظهر الحق ويعلمون ان لأهل السنة ناصرا بالحجة، وكان أكثر مناظرته مع الجبائي المعتزلى وله معه في الظهور عليه مجالس كثيرة فلما كثرت تواليفه ونصر مذهب السنة وبسطه تعلق بها أهل السنة من المالكية والشافعية وبعض الحنفية، فأهل السنة بالمغرب والمشرق بلسانه يتكلمون وبحجته يحتجون، وله من التواليف والتصانيف ما لا يحصى كثرة، وكان ألف في القرآن كتابه الملقب بالمختزن ذكر لى بعض أصحابنا أنه رأى منه طرفا وكان بلغ سورة الكهف وقد انتهى مائة كتاب، ولم يترك آية تعلق بها بدعى إلا أبطل تعلقه بها، وجعلها حجة لأهل الحق وبين المجمل وشرح المشكل، ومن وقف على تواليفه رأى ان الله تعالى قد أمده بمواد توفيقه وأقامه لنصرة الحق والذب عن طريقه، وكان فى مذهبه مالكيا على مذهب أهل الحجاز.
Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Musa ibn Ammar al-Kala'i al-Mayiraqi al-Faqih narrated: The greatest trial was during the time of al-Ma'mun and al-Mu'tasim. Ahmad ibn Hanbal, may Allah be pleased with him, refrained from debating them, so they used that to deceive the rulers and said about them (the People of Sunnah) that they flee from debate because they know their own weakness in supporting falsehood and that they have no proof. They slandered them with that until Ahmad ibn Hanbal and others were put to trial. At that time, the people adopted the saying that the Quran is created, so much so that no witness's testimony was accepted, no judge was appointed, and no mufti gave fatwa unless he said the Quran is created. At that time, there was a group of mutakallimun (speculative theologians) such as Abd al-Aziz al-Makki, al-Harith al-Muhasibi, Abdullah ibn Kullab, and others. They were people of asceticism and piety; none of them would set foot on the carpet of the people of innovation or mix with them. They would refute them and author books to demolish their arguments. Then, after them, and contemporary with some of them in Basra during the days of Isma'il al-Qadi in Baghdad, arose Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Isma'il ibn Abi Bishr al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with him. He authored for the People of Sunnah books on this science, and wrote compilations for them until he demolished the arguments of the Mu'tazila and broke their power. He used to go to them in person to debate. He was spoken to about that and asked: 'How can you mix with the people of innovation and go to them in person, when you have been commanded to avoid them?' He replied: 'They are people of authority; among them are the governor and the judge, and because of their authority they do not come down to me. So if they do not come down to me, and I do not go to them, how can the truth become manifest and they know that the People of Sunnah have a helper by argument?' Most of his debates were with al-Jubba'i the Mu'tazili, and he had many sessions with him in which he triumphed over him. When his writings became numerous and he supported and spread the Sunni school, the People of Sunnah among the Malikis, Shafi'is, and some Hanafis adhered to it. Thus the People of Sunnah in the West and the East speak with his tongue and argue with his proof. His compilations and writings are too numerous to count. He authored a book on the Quran entitled al-Mukhtazan; some of our companions told me they saw a portion of it, and it had reached Surah al-Kahf, and it amounted to one hundred books. He did not leave a single verse that an innovator clung to except he invalidated their clinging to it, and made it a proof for the people of truth, clarified the ambiguous, and explained the problematic. Whoever examines his writings will see that Allah Almighty supplied him with the materials of His success and raised him to support the truth and defend His path. He was, in his school, a Maliki, on the school of the people of the Hijaz.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative describing the early 'Mihna' (inquisition) under the Abbasid caliphs al-Ma'mun and al-Mu'tasim, when the Mu'tazila doctrine of the created Quran was enforced. Ahmad ibn Hanbal famously refused to debate the Mu'tazila, and his stance was used to accuse the Sunni community of fleeing from debate. The pressure was so great that public positions required accepting the createdness of the Quran. During this time, a group of early Sunni mutakallimun—such as Abd al-Aziz al-Makki, al-Harith al-Muhasibi, and Abdullah ibn Kullab—engaged in refuting the Mu'tazila while maintaining asceticism and avoiding direct mixing. Then, after them, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari emerged in Basra, contemporaneous with some of them. He authored works for the Sunnis, refuted the Mu'tazila, and debated them personally. When criticized for associating with innovators, he explained that he had to go to them because they were rulers and would not come to him; only by engaging could the truth prevail. His main opponent was al-Jubba'i, the leading Mu'tazili. Al-Ash'ari's writings became so influential that Sunnis across the Malikis, Shafi'is, and some Hanafis adopted his approach. His work on the Quran, al-Mukhtazan, was a massive commentary refuting innovative interpretations. The passage concludes with praise that Allah granted him success and that he was a Maliki in fiqh.

Key Terms
المحنة
خلق القرآن
المتكلمون
عبد العزيز المكي
الحارث المحاسبي
عبد الله بن كلاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the early Sunni mutakallimun were silent or passive during the Mihna.
Correction: They actively wrote books to demolish the Mu'tazila arguments, though they avoided direct debate.

Checkpoint
Who was the Sunni scholar that refrained from debating the Mu'tazila, leading to accusations of weakness?
A) Abd al-Aziz al-Makki
B) Ahmad ibn Hanbal
C) Al-Harith al-Muhasibi
D) Abdullah ibn Kullab

Key Takeaway
The Mihna forced Sunnis to articulate their beliefs under pressure, and early mutakallimun laid the groundwork for later defenses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face social or institutional pressure to conform to a belief you know is false, do you have the courage of Imam Ahmad to refuse—even when it means being slandered as weak? What would it take for you to stand firm like him?
?
The early mutakallimun combined deep piety with intellectual defense of the faith. Is your own spiritual discipline fueling your ability to defend the truth, or are they disconnected? What is one concrete step you can take to bridge them this week?
?
The Mu'tazila accused the Sunnis of fleeing debate out of weakness. Have you ever avoided defending your faith because you feared you wouldn't have the right answers? What can you learn from the mutakallimun's approach of quiet preparation and written refutation?

Al-Ash'ari's Emergence and Debating Strategy
Ibn Asakir narrates al-Ash'ari's emergence and his approach to debating the Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari emerged as a defender of Sunnah and why he personally engaged Mu'tazila in debate.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari went to the Mu'tazila because they would not come to him.

After the early mutakallimun, a new figure arose: Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. He took a different approach, actively going to the Mu'tazila to debate them. When criticized for mixing with innovators, he gave a compelling justification rooted in the pursuit of truth. This segment captures his distinct methodology and his famous debates with al-Jubba'i.

Guided Path
1
Read about al-Ash'ari's rise
Notice the timeline: after the earlier scholars, al-Ash'ari appeared in Basra and began authoring works for the Sunnis.
He is described as demolishing Mu'tazila arguments.
2
Understand his debating strategy
He would go to them in person. The passage records a question about why he mixes with innovators and his answer.
Focus on his justification: the Mu'tazila held authority and would not descend.
3
Analyze his main debates
His opponents included al-Jubba'i, the leading Mu'tazili. He triumphed in many sessions.
This shows his effectiveness.

Why did al-Ash'ari go to the Mu'tazila to debate?

?

?

?
If you were in al-Ash'ari's place, would you have the courage to go against the common practice of avoidance and engage those in authority? What would need to change in your heart to become that bold?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
