Ibn Furak's Kalam Works up to 320 AH
Ibn Furak enumerates his authored works up to 320 AH.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the vast scope of Ibn Furak's scholarly output in kalam, particularly his refutations of various theological opponents up to the year 320 AH.

Core Idea
Ibn Furak's catalog reveals a theologian tirelessly defending Sunni orthodoxy against all opponents.

This passage from Ibn 'Asakir's Tabyin Kidhb al-Muftari presents a bibliographic list of Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Furak's works. The list, quoted directly from Ibn Furak himself, shows the breadth of his engagement with Mu'tazila, philosophers, materialists, and others. It demonstrates his role as a leading Ash'ari theologian who authored dedicated refutations for each sect.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of books and descriptions
Read the entire list of Ibn Furak's works. Notice the variety of opponents mentioned in the titles and descriptions.
The list is in first-person plural, as if Ibn Furak is speaking.
2
Identify the different opponents
Identify the sects and groups that Ibn Furak refutes: Mu'tazila, philosophers, materialists (dahriyyun), dualists (ahl al-tathniya), atheists (mulhidun), etc.

3
Observe the geographical diversity

This shows scholarly integrity and willingness to correct mistakes.
5
Summarize the impression
After reading the list, summarize what kind of scholar Ibn Furak appears to be. What was his main concern?

كتاب الفنون الذي ألفناه على الملحدين، وألفنا كتابا سميناه ( جواب المصريين ) أتينا فيه على كثير من أبواب الكلام، وألفنا كتابا فى أن العجز عن الشيء غير العجز عن ضده وان ال بجز لا يكون إلا من الموجود نصرنا فيه من قال من أصحابنا بذلك، وألفنا كتابا فيه مسائل على أهل التثنية سميناه كتاب ( المسائل على أهل التثنية ) والفناكتابا مجردا ذكرنا فيه جميع اعتراض الدهريين في قول الموحدين ان الحوادث أولا انها لا تصح وانها لا تصح إلا من محدث وفي أن المحدث واحد وأجبناهم عنه بما فيه اقناع للمسترشدين، وذكرنا أيضا اعتلالات لهم في قدم الأجسام وهذا الكتاب غير كتبنا التي ذكرناها في صدر كتابنا هذا، وه نو مرسوم بالاستقصاء الجميع اعتراض الدهريين وسائر اصناف الملحدين، وألفنا كتابا على الدهريين في اعتلالاتهم فى قدم الأجسام بأنها لا تخلو أن لو كانت محدثة من ان يكون أحدثها لنفسه أو لعلة، وألفنا كتابا نقضنا به اعتراضا على داود بن على الأصبهاني في مسئلة الاعتقاد، وألفنا كتاب ( تفسير القرآن ) رددنا فيه على الجبائي، والبلخى ماحرفا من تأويله(۱) وألفنا كتاب ( زيادات النوادر وألفنا كتابا سميناه (جوابات أهل فارس ) وألفنا كتابا أخبرنا فيه عن اعتلال من زعم أن الموات يفعل بطبعه ونقضنا عليهم اعتلالاتهم وأوضحنا عن تمويههم، وألفنا كتابا في الرؤية نقضنا به اعتراضات اعترض بها علينا الجبائى فى مواضع متفرقة من كتب جمعها محمد بن عمر الصيمري وحكاها عنه، فأبنا عن فسادها وأوضحناه وكشفناه، وألفنا كتابا سميناه (الجوهر في الرد على أهل الزيغ والمنكر) وألفنا كتابا اجبنا فيه عن مسائل الجبائى فى النظر والاستدلال وشرائطه وألفنا كتابا سميناه ( أدب الجدل ) وألفنا كتابا فى مقالات الفلاسفة خاصة وألفنا كتابا في الرد على الفلاسفة يشتمل على ثلاث مقالات ذكرنا فيه نقض علل ابن قيس الدهرى وتكلمنا فيه على القائلين بالهيولى والطبائع ونقضنا فيه علل أرسطو طاليس في السماء والعالم وبينا ما عليهم في قولهم بإضافة الأحداث إلى النجوم وتعليق أحكام السعادة والشقاوة بها .
قال أبو بكر محمد بن فورك هذا هو أسامي كتبه التي ألفها إلى سنة عشرين وثلثمائة، سوى أماليه على الناس والجوابات المتفرقة عن المسائل الواردات من الجهات المختلفات وسوى ما أملاه على الناس مما لم يذكر أسامية ههنا وقد عاش بعد ذلك إلى سنة أربع وعشرين وثلثمائة وصنف فيها كتبا منها كتاب نقض المضاهاة على الاسكافي في التسمية بالقدر وكتاب العمد في الرؤية وكتاب فى معلومات الله ومقدوراته أنه لانهاية لها على أبي الهذيل، وكتاب على حارث الوراق فى الصفات فيما نقض على ابن الراوندى وكتاب على أهل التناسخ وكتاب في الرد في الحركات على أبي الهذيل وكتاب على أهل المنطق ومسائل سئل عنها الجبائي في الأسماء والأحكام ومجالسات في خبر الواحد واثبات القياس، وكتاب في (۱) وغريب من الذهبي ان يزعم ان هذا التفسير مما ألفه علي طريقة الاعتزال، وأنت ترى انه ما ألفه إلا للرد على المعتزلة، ويقع للذهبي امثال هذا في تراجم المتكلمين من أهل السنة سامحه الله .
The Mu'tazila, and we authored a book we named 'Answer of the Damascenes' on subtleties of kalam, and we authored a book we named 'Answer of the Wasitians' on branches of kalam, and we authored a book we named 'Answers of the Ramhurmuzians' – and some of the Mu'tazila from Ramhurmuz wrote to me asking for a response to questions that were circulating in his mind, so I answered them. And we authored a book we named 'The Scattered Baghdadi Questions' and in it are sessions that took place between us and the leaders of the Mu'tazila. And we authored a book we named 'The Selected' on the scattered Basran questions. And we authored a book I named the 'Book of Arts' in refutation of the atheists. And I authored 'The Book of Rarities' on the intricacies of kalam. And I authored a book I named the 'Book of Perception' on branches of the subtleties of kalam. And I authored a refutation of the book known as 'al-Latif' against al-Iskafi. And I authored a book in which I refuted the speech of 'Abbad ibn Sulayman on the intricacies of kalam. And I authored a book in which I refuted a book authored by 'Ali ibn 'Isa. And we authored a book on types of kalam we named 'The Repository' in which we mentioned questions of the opponents that they did not ask us about, nor write in their books, nor set out to question, and we answered them with what Allah Almighty guided us to. And we authored a book on the topic of 'thing' and that things are things even if they cease to exist; we retracted it and refuted it, so whoever comes across it should not rely on it. And we authored a book on ijtihad in rulings. And we authored a book that analogy specifies the apparent meaning of the Qur'an. And we authored a subtle book on the means of knowledge. And we authored a book on reports and their specification. And we authored a book we named 'The Arts' on chapters of kalam, distinct from the 'Book of Arts' we authored against the atheists. And we authored a book we named 'Answer of the Egyptians' in which we covered many chapters of kalam. And we authored a book that incapacity for a thing is not incapacity for its opposite, and that incapacity only arises from the existent (al-mawjud); in it we supported those of our companions who said that. And we authored a book containing questions against the dualists, we named it 'The Book of Questions against the Dualists'. And we authored an independent book in which we mentioned all the objections of the materialists (al-dahriyyun) regarding the statement of the monotheists that temporal events (al-hawadith) are first – that they are not valid, and that they are only valid from an originator (muhdith), and that the originator is one – and we answered them with what is convincing to seekers of guidance. And we also mentioned their arguments for the pre-eternity of bodies, and this book is other than our books we mentioned at the beginning of this our book, and it is titled 'al-Istiqsa' encompassing all the objections of the materialists and all types of atheists. And we authored a book against the materialists on their arguments for the pre-eternity of bodies, that they are not free from, if they were originated, either being originated by themselves or by a cause. And we authored a book in which we refuted an objection against Dawud ibn 'Ali al-Isbahani on the issue of belief. And we authored the 'Book of Interpretation of the Qur'an' in which we refuted al-Jubba'i and al-Balkhi, [refuting] every distortion of his interpretation(1). And we authored the 'Book of Additions to the Rarities'. And we authored a book we named 'Answers of the People of Persia'. And we authored a book in which we informed about the argument of one who claimed that lifeless things act by their nature, and we refuted their arguments and exposed their obfuscation. And we authored a book on the vision (al-ru'ya) in which we refuted objections raised against us by al-Jubba'i in scattered places of books collected by Muhammad ibn 'Umar al-Saymari and narrated from him; so we explained their corruption, clarified and uncovered them. And we authored a book we named 'The Jewel in Refutation of the People of Deviation and Denial'. And we authored a book in which we answered questions of al-Jubba'i on speculation (al-nazar) and inference (al-istidlal) and their conditions. And we authored a book we named 'The Etiquette of Disputation'. And we authored a book specifically on the doctrines of the philosophers. And we authored a book in refutation of the philosophers comprising three articles, in which we mentioned the refutation of the causes of Ibn Qays al-Dahri, and we spoke against the proponents of hyle (al-hayula) and natures, and we refuted therein the causes of Aristotle regarding the heavens and the world, and we made clear what is against them in their statement attributing events to the stars and attaching the judgments of happiness and misery to them.
Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Furak said: These are the names of his books which he authored up to the year 320 AH, apart from his dictations (amali) to the people and the scattered answers to questions coming from various regions, and apart from what he dictated to the people whose names are not mentioned here. And he lived after that until the year 324 AH, and he authored in it books including: the book 'Refutation of al-Mudaha' against al-Iskafi on the designation of al-Qadir; and the book 'al-'Amad on the Vision'; and a book on Allah's objects of knowledge and His objects of power that they have no end, against Abu al-Hudhayl; and a book against Harith al-Warraq on the attributes, concerning what he refuted against Ibn al-Rawandi; and a book against the proponents of metempsychosis (al-tanasukh); and a book on the refutation of movements against Abu al-Hudhayl; and a book against the logicians; and questions asked of al-Jubba'i on names and rulings; and sessions on the solitary report (khabar al-wahid) and the proof of analogy (al-qiyas); and a book on (1) And it is strange of al-Dhahabi to claim that this interpretation was authored on the method of i'tizal, whereas you see that he only authored it to refute the Mu'tazila. And similar things occur to al-Dhahabi in the biographies of Sunni theologians – Allah forgive him.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographic catalog of the works of Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Furak, a prominent Ash'ari theologian, as compiled by Ibn 'Asakir in his Tabyin Kidhb al-Muftari. The text begins with a first-person plural account (likely quoting Ibn Furak himself) listing numerous books he authored, primarily in the field of kalam (dialectical theology), refuting various sects such as the Mu'tazila, materialists (dahriyyun), philosophers, dualists, and atheists. The list includes works like 'Answer of the Damascenes', 'Answer of the Wasitians', 'The Scattered Baghdadi Questions', and many others, each addressing specific theological topics or responding to particular opponents. The author also mentions retracting and refuting one of his own books on the topic of 'thing' (shay'), warning readers not to rely on it. The catalog then transitions to a third-person statement by Ibn Furak himself (introduced by 'قال أبو بكر محمد بن فورك') summarizing that these are the names of his books up to 320 AH, excluding his dictation sessions and scattered answers. He also notes that he lived until 324 AH and authored additional works in that period, such as a refutation of al-Iskafi's concept of al-Qadir, a book on the vision of Allah, and works against Abu al-Hudhayl, Ibn al-Rawandi, and the logicians. The passage concludes with an editorial note criticizing al-Dhahabi's claim that Ibn Furak's Tafsir was written from a Mu'tazili perspective, asserting that it was actually written to refute the Mu'tazila. The passage is primarily a straightforward list, but it provides valuable insight into the scope and range of Ibn Furak's scholarly output and his role as a defender of Sunni orthodoxy.

Checkpoint
What was the purpose of Ibn Furak's book 'al-Mukhtazan'?
A) To summarize his earlier works
B) To refute the Mu'tazila
C) To answer questions that opponents never asked
D) To explain the nature of things

Key Takeaway
Ibn Furak's catalog shows him as a prolific defender of Sunni theology, addressing every major rival school of his time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ibn Furak dedicated his life to writing refutations of theological errors. What confusion or false belief about Islam do you see spreading in your own community, and what are you actively doing to counter it—or are you content to remain silent?
?
He authored a book, then retracted and refuted it himself, warning others not to rely on it. Is there a belief or habit you once held that you now know is wrong? Have you taken the step to publicly correct it, or are you still clinging to it out of pride?
?
His works engaged every major opponent of Sunni Islam in his time. Are there intellectual challenges to your faith (e.g., atheism, relativism, scientism) that you have avoided studying? What specific step will you take this week to learn how to respond to one of them?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
5 min
Later Works and the Tafsir's True Purpose
Ibn Furak summarizes his works and lists later books; editor corrects al-Dhahabi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the additional works Ibn Furak authored after 320 AH and the corrective purpose of his Tafsir against Mu'tazili interpretations.

Core Idea
Ibn Furak's later works continued his defense of orthodoxy, and his Tafsir was a refutation, not an adoption, of Mu'tazilism.

This concluding part of the catalog provides Ibn Furak's own summary of his output up to 320 AH and lists further works composed in the remaining years of his life. It also includes an editorial remark by Ibn 'Asakir correcting a misattribution by al-Dhahabi, clarifying that Ibn Furak's Tafsir was written against al-Jubba'i, not in support of him.

Guided Path
1
Read Ibn Furak's summary statement
Read the passage from 'قال أبو بكر محمد بن فورك' onward. Note how he distinguishes his listed books from other teachings and dictations.
2
Identify the later books
Identify the books he authored after 320 AH, including refutations of al-Iskafi, Abu al-Hudhayl, and others.
He lived until 324 AH, so these are his final works.
3
Understand the editor's correction
Read the editor's comment about al-Dhahabi's claim. What is the editor saying about the nature of Ibn Furak's Tafsir?
The editor strongly refutes the idea that the Tafsir was Mu'tazili.
4
Reflect on the significance
Why is it important to clarify that Ibn Furak's Tafsir was a refutation? What does it tell us about his theological stance?
This reinforces his identity as a Sunni orthodox theologian.

المعتزلة، وألفنا كتابا سميناه ( جواب الدمشقيين) في لطائف من الكلام، والفنا كتابا سميناه ) جواب الواسطيين فى فنون من الكلام، وألفنا كتابا سميناه ) جوابات (الرامهرمزيين) وكان بعض المعتزلة من رامهرمز كتب إلى يسألنى الجواب عن مسائل كانت تدور فى نفسه فأجبت عنها، وألفنا كتابا سميناه ( المسائل المنثورة البغدادية ) وفيه مجالس دارت بيننا وبين اعلام المعتزلة، وألفنا كتابا سميناه ( المنتخل ) فى المسائل المنثورات البصريات والفنا كتابا سميته كتاب ( الفنون ) فى الرد على الملحدين، وألفت كتاب النوادر في دقائق الكلام، وألفت كتابا سميته كتاب ( الادراك ) في فنون من لطائف الكلام، وألفت نقض الكتاب المعروف باللطيف على الاسكافي، وألفت كتابا نقضت فيه كلام عباد بن سليمان في دقائق الكلام، وألفت كتابا نقضت فيه كتابا على على بن عيسى من تأليفه، وألفنا كتابا في ضروب من الكلام سميناه ( المختزن) ذكرنا فيه مسائل للمخالفين لم يسألونا عنها ولاسطروها في كتبهم ولم يتجهوا للسؤال وأجبنا عنها بما وفقنا الله تعالى له، وألفنا كتابا فى باب شيء وان الأشياء هى أشياء وان عدمت رجعنا عنه ونقضناه فمن وقع اليه فلا يعولن عليه، وألفنا كتابا في الاجتهاد في الأحكام، وألفنا كتابا فى ان القياس يخص ظاهر القرآن، وألفنا كتابا في المعارف لطيفا، وألفنا كتابا في الأخبار وتخصيصها وألفنا كتابا سميناه ( الفنون ) فى أبواب من الكلام غير كتاب الفنون الذي ألفناه على الملحدين، وألفنا كتابا سميناه ( جواب المصريين ) أتينا فيه على كثير من أبواب الكلام، وألفنا كتابا فى أن العجز عن الشيء غير العجز عن ضده وان ال بجز لا يكون إلا من الموجود نصرنا فيه من قال من أصحابنا بذلك، وألفنا كتابا فيه مسائل على أهل التثنية سميناه كتاب ( المسائل على أهل التثنية ) والفناكتابا مجردا ذكرنا فيه جميع اعتراض الدهريين في قول الموحدين ان الحوادث أولا انها لا تصح وانها لا تصح إلا من محدث وفي أن المحدث واحد وأجبناهم عنه بما فيه اقناع للمسترشدين، وذكرنا أيضا اعتلالات لهم في قدم الأجسام وهذا الكتاب غير كتبنا التي ذكرناها في صدر كتابنا هذا، وه نو مرسوم وألفنا كتابا أخبرنا فيه عن اعتلال من زعم أن الموات يفعل بطبعه ونقضنا عليهم اعتلالاتهم وأوضحنا عن تمويههم، وألفنا كتابا في الرؤية نقضنا به اعتراضات اعترض بها علينا الجبائى فى مواضع متفرقة من كتب جمعها قال أبو بكر محمد بن فورك هذا هو أسامي كتبه التي ألفها إلى سنة عشرين وثلثمائة، سوى أماليه على الناس والجوابات المتفرقة عن المسائل الواردات من الجهات المختلفات وسوى ما أملاه على الناس مما لم يذكر أسامية ههنا وقد عاش بعد ذلك إلى سنة أربع وعشرين وثلثمائة وصنف فيها كتبا منها كتاب نقض المضاهاة على الاسكافي في التسمية بالقدر وكتاب العمد في الرؤية وكتاب فى معلومات الله ومقدوراته أنه لانهاية لها على أبي الهذيل، وكتاب على حارث الوراق فى الصفات فيما نقض على ابن الراوندى وكتاب على أهل التناسخ وكتاب في الرد في الحركات على أبي الهذيل وكتاب على أهل المنطق ومسائل سئل عنها الجبائي في الأسماء والأحكام ومجالسات في خبر الواحد واثبات القياس، وكتاب في (۱) وغريب من الذهبي ان يزعم ان هذا التفسير مما ألفه علي طريقة الاعتزال، وأنت ترى انه ما ألفه إلا للرد على المعتزلة، ويقع للذهبي امثال هذا في تراجم المتكلمين من أهل السنة سامحه الله .

And we authored the 'Book of Interpretation of the Qur'an' in which we refuted al-Jubba'i and al-Balkhi, [refuting] every distortion of his interpretation(1). And we authored the 'Book of Additions to the Rarities'. And we authored a book we named 'Answers of the People of Persia'. And we authored a book in which we informed about the argument of one who claimed that lifeless things act by their nature, and we refuted their arguments and exposed their obfuscation. And we authored a book on the vision (al-ru'ya) in which we refuted objections raised against us by al-Jubba'i in scattered places of books collected by Muhammad ibn 'Umar al-Saymari and narrated from him; so we explained their corruption, clarified and uncovered them. And we authored a book we named 'The Jewel in Refutation of the People of Deviation and Denial'. And we authored a book in which we answered questions of al-Jubba'i on speculation (al-nazar) and inference (al-istidlal) and their conditions. And we authored a book we named 'The Etiquette of Disputation'. And we authored a book specifically on the doctrines of the philosophers. And we authored a book in refutation of the philosophers comprising three articles, in which we mentioned the refutation of the causes of Ibn Qays al-Dahri, and we spoke against the proponents of hyle (al-hayula) and natures, and we refuted therein the causes of Aristotle regarding the heavens and the world, and we made clear what is against them in their statement attributing events to the stars and attaching the judgments of happiness and misery to them.
Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Furak said: These are the names of his books which he authored up to the year 320 AH, apart from his dictations (amali) to the people and the scattered answers to questions coming from various regions, and apart from what he dictated to the people whose names are not mentioned here. And he lived after that until the year 324 AH, and he authored in it books including: the book 'Refutation of al-Mudaha' against al-Iskafi on the designation of al-Qadir; and the book 'al-'Amad on the Vision'; and a book on Allah's objects of knowledge and His objects of power that they have no end, against Abu al-Hudhayl; and a book against Harith al-Warraq on the attributes, concerning what he refuted against Ibn al-Rawandi; and a book against the proponents of metempsychosis (al-tanasukh); and a book on the refutation of movements against Abu al-Hudhayl; and a book against the logicians; and questions asked of al-Jubba'i on names and rulings; and sessions on the solitary report (khabar al-wahid) and the proof of analogy (al-qiyas); and a book on (1) And it is strange of al-Dhahabi to claim that this interpretation was authored on the method of i'tizal, whereas you see that he only authored it to refute the Mu'tazila. And similar things occur to al-Dhahabi in the biographies of Sunni theologians – Allah forgive him.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographic catalog of the works of Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Furak, a prominent Ash'ari theologian, as compiled by Ibn 'Asakir in his Tabyin Kidhb al-Muftari. The text begins with a first-person plural account (likely quoting Ibn Furak himself) listing numerous books he authored, primarily in the field of kalam (dialectical theology), refuting various sects such as the Mu'tazila, materialists (dahriyyun), philosophers, dualists, and atheists. The list includes works like 'Answer of the Damascenes', 'Answer of the Wasitians', 'The Scattered Baghdadi Questions', and many others, each addressing specific theological topics or responding to particular opponents. The author also mentions retracting and refuting one of his own books on the topic of 'thing' (shay'), warning readers not to rely on it. The catalog then transitions to a third-person statement by Ibn Furak himself (introduced by 'قال أبو بكر محمد بن فورك') summarizing that these are the names of his books up to 320 AH, excluding his dictation sessions and scattered answers. He also notes that he lived until 324 AH and authored additional works in that period, such as a refutation of al-Iskafi's concept of al-Qadir, a book on the vision of Allah, and works against Abu al-Hudhayl, Ibn al-Rawandi, and the logicians. The passage concludes with an editorial note criticizing al-Dhahabi's claim that Ibn Furak's Tafsir was written from a Mu'tazili perspective, asserting that it was actually written to refute the Mu'tazila. The passage is primarily a straightforward list, but it provides valuable insight into the scope and range of Ibn Furak's scholarly output and his role as a defender of Sunni orthodoxy.

Correction: The passage clarifies that he wrote it to refute al-Jubba'i and al-Balkhi, thus it is a Sunni refutation.

Checkpoint

A) To interpret the Qur'an according to Mu'tazili views
B) To refute al-Jubba'i and al-Balkhi's interpretations
C) To support al-Ash'ari's methodology

Key Takeaway
Ibn Furak's later works and the editorial note confirm his unwavering opposition to Mu'tazilism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a claim about a scholar's position (like al-Dhahabi's claim about Ibn Furak), do you take the time to verify it from primary sources, or do you rely on secondary accounts? What is one such claim you have accepted without verification?
?
The editor did not hesitate to correct a respected figure like al-Dhahabi. If you find that a teacher or author you admire made a factual error, would you have the courage to check and correct it? What holds you back?
?
Ibn Furak dedicated his later works to refuting errors. What is one error in your own understanding of Aqeedah that you have identified but not yet thoroughly uprooted? What specific step will you take this week to address it?

Al-Ash'ari's Early Works: A Bibliographic Overview
List of al-Ash'ari's early writings as reported by Ibn Furak.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scope and variety of al-Ash'ari's early writings as catalogued by Ibn Furak.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari authored a diverse range of works refuting Mu'tazilites, philosophers, and others.

In this passage, Ibn Furak provides a list of works composed by Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari up to the year 320 AH. These writings range from Quranic exegesis to refutations of philosophers and theological opponents. As we read, pay attention to the diversity of subjects and the opponents addressed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to get an overview of the list of books. Do not analyze yet, just absorb the breadth of works.
2
Identify the main works
Note the titles and their subjects: Tafsir, book on ru'ya, refutations of al-Jubba'i, philosophers, etc. See how al-Ash'ari addresses different opponents.
3
Recognize the opponents
Al-Ash'ari refutes specific individuals like al-Jubba'i, Dawud al-Asbahani, and groups like philosophers and materialists. This shows his engagement with various schools.
4
Reflect on the scope
Consider that this is only a partial list up to 320 AH, excluding oral dictations and scattered responses. It indicates his prolific output.
Ibn Furak mentions that these are the named books only.

If it were created, either it would have originated from itself or from a cause. And we authored a book by which we refuted an objection against Dawud ibn 'Ali al-Asbahani regarding the issue of belief. And we authored the book 'Tafsir al-Qur'an' in which we refuted al-Jubba'i and al-Balkhi regarding their distortion of its interpretation. And we authored the book 'Ziyadat al-Nawadir'. And we authored a book we named 'Jawabat Ahl Faris'. And we authored a book in which we informed about the reasoning of those who claim that inanimate objects act by their nature, and we refuted their arguments and clarified their obfuscation. And we authored a book on the vision (of God) by which we refuted objections raised against us by al-Jubba'i in various scattered places in books collected by Muhammad ibn 'Umar al-Saymari and related on his authority; we exposed their corruption and clarified and unveiled it. And we authored a book in which we answered al-Jubba'i's questions on speculation (al-nazar) and inference (al-istidlal) and their conditions. And we authored a book we named 'Adab al-Jadal'. And we authored a book specifically on the opinions of the philosophers. Ibn Furak concludes by noting that these are the titled works, excluding oral dictations and scattered answers. The passage highlights al-Ash'ari's extensive scholarly output in defending orthodox doctrine against various opponents.

Al-Ash'ari's Theological Polemics (320-324 AH)
List of al-Ash'ari's polemical works against heretics and philosophers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the wide range of theological controversies al-Ash'ari engaged with in his final years, including refutations of Mu'tazilites, philosophers, and heretics.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's later works show him as a tireless defender of Sunni orthodoxy against multiple fronts.

This passage from Ibn Furak's biography lists al-Ash'ari's works written between 320 and 324 AH. The sheer variety of topics—predestination, vision of God, infinity of divine knowledge, metempsychosis—demonstrates his engagement with every major theological issue of his time. Let's examine these works to see how al-Ash'ari systematically rebutted his opponents.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of works against Mu'tazilite figures
Identify works targeting Abu al-Hudhayl, al-Askafi, and al-Jubba'i. Note the specific topics: predestination (qadar), vision of God (ru'ya), divine attributes.
2
Identify specific heresies refuted
Al-Ash'ari wrote against the Qadariyya (free will), the Mu'tazilite denial of ru'ya, the infinity of divine objects, and metempsychosis (tanasukh).
These were live debates in the early 4th century AH.
3
Notice the variety of opponents
Beyond Mu'tazilites, he refuted logicians, philosophers (Aristotelians), and proponents of tanasukh.
4
Reflect on his method
Each work is a focused refutation, showing al-Ash'ari's systematic approach to defending Sunni theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد عاش بعد ذلك إلى سنة أربع وعشرين وثلثمائة وصنف فيها كتبا منها كتاب نقض المضاهاة على الاسكافي في التسمية بالقدر وكتاب العمد في الرؤية وكتاب فى معلومات الله ومقدوراته أنه لانهاية لها على أبي الهذيل، وكتاب على حارث الوراق فى الصفات فيما نقض على ابن الراوندى وكتاب على أهل التناسخ وكتاب في الرد في الحركات على أبي الهذيل وكتاب على أهل المنطق ومسائل سئل عنها الجبائي في الأسماء والأحكام ومجالسات في خبر الواحد واثبات القياس، وكتاب في أفعال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم تسليما، وكتاب في الوقوف والعموم، وكتاب في متشابه القرآن جمع فيه بين المعتزلة والملحدين فيما يطعنون به في متشابه الحديث ونقض كتاب التاج على ابن الراوندي وكتاب فيه بيان مذهب النصارى وكتاب فى الامامة، وكتاب فيه الكلام على النصارى مما يحتج به عليهم من سائر الكتب التي يعترفون بها وكتاب في النقض على ابن الراوندى فى إبطال التواتر وفيما يتعلق به الطاعنون على التواتر ومسائل في إثبات الاجماع، وكتاب في حكايات مذاهب المجسمة وما يحتجون به وكتاب نقض شرح الكتاب وكتاب في مسائل جرت بينه وبين أبي الفرج المالكي فى علة الخمر ونقض كتاب آثار العلوية على ارسطو طاليس وكتاب في جوابات مسائل لأبى هاشم استملاها ابن أبي صالح الطبري وكتابه الذي سماه (الاحتجاج) وكتاب ( الاخبار ) الذى أملاه على البرهان وذلك آخر ما بلغنا من اسامى تصانيفه وله كتاب فى دلائل النبوة مفرد وكتاب آخر في الامامة مفرد
And he lived after that until the year 324 AH, and he authored books in it, including: the book 'Naqd al-Mudahah' against al-Askafi regarding the naming of predestination (qadar), and the book 'al-'Amd fi al-Ru'ya', and the book on God's known things and objects of power that they are infinite, against Abu al-Hudhayl, and the book against Harith al-Warraq on the attributes, regarding what was refuted against Ibn al-Rawandi, and the book against the proponents of metempsychosis (tanasukh), and the book on the refutation of movements against Abu al-Hudhayl, and the book against the logicians, and questions asked of al-Jubba'i on names and rulings, and sessions (mujalasat) on the solitary report (khabar al-wahid) and the affirmation of analogical reasoning (qiyas), and the book on the actions of the Prophet, peace be upon him, as a submission, and the book on pauses (wuquf) and generality (umum), and the book on the ambiguous verses of the Qur'an in which he brought together the Mu'tazilites and the heretics regarding their criticisms of the ambiguous hadith, and the refutation of the book 'al-Taj' against Ibn al-Rawandi, and a book containing an exposition of the Christian doctrine, and a book on the imamate, and a book containing speech against the Christians by arguments from all the books they acknowledge, and a book on the refutation of Ibn al-Rawandi doctrines of the corporealists (mujassima) and their arguments, and the refutation of the explanation of the book, and a book on questions that occurred between him and Abu al-Faraj al-Maliki on the cause of wine, and the refutation of the book 'Athar al-'Alawiyya' against Aristotle, and a book in response to questions for Abu Hashim which Ibn Abi Salih al-Tabari transcribed, and his book called 'al-Ihtijaj', and the book 'al-Akhbar' which he dictated on al-Burhan, and that is the last we have reached of the names of his compilations. And he has a separate book on the proofs of prophethood and another separate book on the imamate.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage continues Ibn Furak's account of al-Ash'ari's works, focusing on those written between 320 and 324 AH. The list shows al-Ash'ari's engagement with a wide range of theological and philosophical issues: refutations of predestinarian views, discussions on the vision of God, the infinity of God's knowledge, responses to Mu'tazilites like Abu al-Hudhayl and al-Jubba'i, critiques of Ibn al-Rawandi, treatises on logic, metempsychosis, the actions of the Prophet, ambiguous texts, consensus, and polemics against Christians and corporealists. The inclusion of works on the imamate and proofs of prophethood indicates his broader concerns. The passage concludes by noting that this is the extent of Ibn Furak's knowledge of al-Ash'ari's authored works.

Al-Ash'ari's Works on Usul, Hadith, and Interfaith
List of al-Ash'ari's works on usul, hadith, interfaith, and concluding notes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ash'ari's contributions to usul al-fiqh, hadith sciences, and interfaith polemics as documented in his later works.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari did not limit himself to theology; he also wrote on legal theory, consensus, and Christian doctrine.

The second part of Ibn Furak's list reveals al-Ash'ari's broader scholarly interests. Here we find works on the solitary report (khabar al-wahid), analogical reasoning (qiyas), consensus (ijma'), and even a refutation of Christian teachings. This shows that al-Ash'ari's legacy extends beyond kalam into the foundations of Islamic law and interfaith debate.

Guided Path
1
Scan the list for works related to usul

2
Note the books on ambiguous texts
He wrote on mutashabih al-Qur'an and mutashabih al-hadith, addressing hermeneutical challenges.
This shows engagement with textual interpretation.
3
Identify interfaith works
There are two works against Christianity and one on imamate, showing polemical and political concerns.
4
Consider the final note
Ibn Furak says this is the last he knew of al-Ash'ari's works, including separate books on prophethood and imamate.
This marks the end of al-Ash'ari's known bibliography.

was refuted against Ibn al-Rawandi, and the book against the proponents of metempsychosis (tanasukh), and the book on the refutation of movements against Abu al-Hudhayl, and the book against the logicians, and questions asked of al-Jubba'i on names and rulings, and sessions (mujalasat) on the solitary report (khabar al-wahid) and the affirmation of analogical reasoning (qiyas), and the book on the actions of the Prophet, peace be upon him, as a submission, and the book on pauses (wuquf) and generality (umum), and the book on the ambiguous verses of the Qur'an in which he brought together the Mu'tazilites and the heretics regarding their criticisms of the ambiguous hadith, and the refutation of the book 'al-Taj' against Ibn al-Rawandi, and a book containing an exposition of the Christian doctrine, and a book on the imamate, and a book containing speech against the Christians by arguments from all the books they acknowledge, and a book on the refutation of Ibn al-Rawandi regarding the invalidation of recurrent transmission (tawatur) and what the critics of tawatur rely on, and questions on the affirmation of consensus (ijma'), and a book on the narratives of the doctrines of the corporealists (mujassima) and their arguments, and the refutation of the explanation of the book, and a book on questions that occurred between him and Abu al-Faraj al-Maliki on the cause of wine, and the refutation of the book 'Athar al-'Alawiyya' against Aristotle, and a book in response to questions for Abu Hashim which Ibn Abi Salih al-Tabari transcribed, and his book called 'al-Ihtijaj', and the book 'al-Akhbar' which he dictated on al-Burhan, and that is the last we have reached of the names of his compilations. And he has a separate book on the proofs of prophethood and another separate book on the imamate.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage continues Ibn Furak's account of al-Ash'ari's works, focusing on those written between 320 and 324 AH. The list shows al-Ash'ari's engagement with a wide range of theological and philosophical issues: refutations of predestinarian views, discussions on the vision of God, the infinity of God's knowledge, responses to Mu'tazilites like Abu al-Hudhayl and al-Jubba'i, critiques of Ibn al-Rawandi, treatises on logic, metempsychosis, the actions of the Prophet, ambiguous texts, consensus, and polemics against Christians and corporealists. The inclusion of works on the imamate and proofs of prophethood indicates his broader concerns. The passage concludes by noting that this is the extent of Ibn Furak's knowledge of al-Ash'ari's authored works.

القياس
التواتر

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's works extend beyond theology to include usul al-fiqh, hadith sciences, and interfaith polemics, showing his comprehensive scholarship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
He wrote against Christians using their own scriptures. Do you know enough about other faiths to defend Islam when needed? What practical step will you take this week to learn about Christian or Jewish beliefs?
?
Al-Ash'ari defended the consensus (ijma') of scholars. In your daily life, when you disagree with scholarly consensus, do you humble yourself or cling to your own view? How will you cultivate reliance on collective scholarship rather than personal opinion starting today?

Ibn Asakir's Additions on al-Ash'ari's Works
Ibn Asakir supplements Ibn Furak's list with more works and an anecdotal report

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Ibn Asakir supplements Ibn Furak's list of al-Ash'ari's works, highlighting additional titles and an anecdote that underscores al-Ash'ari's vast scholarly output.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari authored over 300 works—his legacy is immense.

Ibn Asakir continues his biographical account by adding works not catalogued by Ibn Furak. He also shares a remarkable anecdote: a reliable source counted over three hundred titles in al-Ash'ari's indexes. This passage gives us a glimpse into the sheer volume of al-Ash'ari's scholarly production and his mastery of various sciences.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: first a list of additional works, then an anecdote, then a concluding remark on the Tafsir.
2
Identify the additional works
Ibn Asakir mentions three specific works not in Ibn Furak's list: an epistle encouraging inquiry, an epistle on the definition of faith, and answers to questions from the frontier region. Find these in the text.
These titles show the breadth of al-Ash'ari's writing.
3
Reflect on the anecdote and its significance
The anecdote reports that al-Ash'ari's indexes contained over 300 works. Consider why Ibn Asakir includes this—it emphasizes al-Ash'ari's immense learning and counters any underestimation of his output.
The remark about the Tafsir's introduction further cements his scholarly excellence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ الامام الحافظ رضى الله عنه هذا آخر ماذكره أبو بكر بن فورك من تصانيفه وقد وقع إلى أشياء لم يذكرها في تسمية تواليفه فمنها رسالة (الحث على البحث ) ورسالة فى الايمان وهل يطلق عليه اسم الخلق وجواب مسائل كتب بها إلى أهل الثغر في تبيين ماسألوه عنه من مذهب أهل الحق، وأخبرني الشيخ أبو القاسم بن نصر الواعظ في كتابه عن أبي المعالى بن عبدالملك القاضي قال سمعت من أثق به قال رأيت تراجم کتب الامام أبي الحسن فعددتها أكثر من مائتين وثلثمائة مصنف وفي ذلك ما يدل على سعة علمه وينبيء الجاهل به عن غزارة فهمه . وخطبته في أول كتابه الذى صنفه في تفسير القرآن أدل دليل على تبريزه في العلم به علی الأقران وهو الذي سماه تفسير القرآن والرد على من خالف البيان من
The Sheikh, the Imam, the Hafiz, may God be pleased with him, said: This is the end of what Abu Bakr ibn Furak mentioned of his compilations. And I have come across things that he did not mention in his list of his works, among them: the epistle 'al-Hathth 'ala al-Bahth' (Encouragement of Inquiry), and an epistle on faith and whether the term 'creation' is applied to it, and answers to questions written to the people of al-Thaghr explaining what they asked about regarding the doctrine of the People of Truth. And Sheikh Abu al-Qasim ibn Nasr al-Wa'iz informed me in his book on the authority of Abu al-Ma'ali ibn 'Abd al-Malik al-Qadi who said: I heard from someone I trust who said: I saw the indexes of the books of Imam Abu al-Hasan and I counted them as more than three hundred and two hundred works (i.e., more than 300). In that is evidence of the breadth of his knowledge, and it informs the ignorant about the abundance of his understanding. And his introduction (khutba) at the beginning of his book which he wrote on the interpretation of the Qur'an is the clearest evidence of his excellence in knowledge over his peers. It is the one he named 'Tafsir al-Qur'an wa al-Radd 'ala man Khalaf al-Bayan min' (Interpretation of the Qur'an and Refutation of those who Opposed the Clear Statement from...)
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is Ibn Asakir's own supplement to Ibn Furak's list. He notes that he has found additional works not mentioned by Ibn Furak, such as an epistle encouraging inquiry, one on the definition of faith, and responses to questions from the frontier region about the Sunni creed. He then reports an anecdote from a trustworthy source that the indexes of al-Ash'ari's books numbered over 300 works, emphasizing his vast learning. Finally, he highlights the introduction to al-Ash'ari's Tafsir as proof of his superiority in knowledge. The passage underscores the immense scholarly output of al-Ash'ari and the esteem in which he was held.

Key Terms
الحث على البحث
الايمان
أهل الثغر
تراجم الكتب
تفسير القرآن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ibn Furak's list of al-Ash'ari's works is exhaustive.
Correction: Ibn Asakir shows that there were many more works not catalogued by Ibn Furak, such as the epistle on inquiry and others, and that the total number exceeded 300.

Al-Ash'ari's Conversion and Scholarly Output
Al-Ash'ari's conversion and book production

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ash'ari's intellectual journey from Mu'tazilism to Sunni orthodoxy and his vast scholarly output.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari repented from Mu'tazilism and wrote extensively to refute his former views.

This lesson focuses on the first part of the passage, which describes al-Ash'ari's many books and his conversion from the Mu'tazila. It highlights how his repentance led him to produce a refutation of his own earlier work, demonstrating his intellectual integrity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on al-Ash'ari's books
Read the Arabic passage that mentions his nearly 200 books and the 'al-Mujaz al-Kabir'. Notice the scope of his work.
2
Understand his conversion
Identify the sequence: he initially believed in the Mu'tazila, then Allah showed him their misguidance, so he wrote a refutation of his own previous book.
This shows his commitment to truth.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself why this conversion is important for Ahl al-Sunnah. It marks al-Ash'ari as a defender of orthodoxy after being an adversary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد وجدت الحسن الأشعرى رضى الله عنه كتبا كثيرة فى هذا الفن وهي قريبة من مائتى كتاب والموجز الكبير يأتي على عامة ما في كتبه وقد صنف الأشعرى كتابا كبيرا لتصحيح مذهب المعتزلة فإنه كان يعتقد مذهب المعتزلة فى الابتداء، ثم ان الله تعالى بين له ضلالهم فبان عما اعتقده من مذهبهم وصنف كتابا ناقضا لما صنف للمعتزلة، وقد أخد عامة أصحاب الشافعي بما استقر عليه مذهب أبي الحسن الأشعرى وصنف أصحاب الشافعي كتبا كثيرة على وفق ما ذهب إليه الأشعرى إلا أن بعض أصحابنا من أهل السنة والجماعة خطأ أبا الحسن الأشعرى في بعض المسائل مثل قوله التكوين والمكون واحد ونحوها على ما يبين فى خلال المسائل ان شاء الله تعالى فمن وقف على المسائل التي أخطأ فيها أبو الحسن وعرف خطأه فلا بأس له بالنظر في كتبه فقد امسك كتبه كثير من أصحابنا من أهل السنة والجماعة ونظروا فيها .
And I found that al-Hasan al-Ash'ari (may Allah be pleased with him) had many books in this field, nearly two hundred books, and the 'al-Mujaz al-Kabir' covers most of what is in his books. And al-Ash'ari authored a large book to correct the doctrine of the Mu'tazila, for he initially believed in the doctrine of the Mu'tazila. Then Allah, the Exalted, showed him their misguidance, so he disassociated himself from their doctrine and authored a book refuting what he had authored for the Mu'tazila. And the majority of the companions of al-Shafi'i adopted the settled doctrine of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. And the companions of al-Shafi'i authored many books in accordance with what al-Ash'ari held, except that some of our associates from Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah considered Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari to be mistaken in some issues, such as his statement that 'al-takwin and al-mukawwan are one' and similar matters, as will be explained in the course of the issues, if Allah wills. So whoever comes across the issues in which Abu al-Hasan erred and recognizes his error, there is no harm for him in looking at his books. For many of our associates from Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah have kept his books and looked into them.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage provides an overview of al-Ash'ari's scholarly output and his doctrinal journey. The author states that al-Ash'ari wrote nearly 200 books on kalam, with the 'al-Mujaz al-Kabir' summarizing them. Initially a Mu'tazili, al-Ash'ari wrote a book to defend their position, but after Allah showed him their error, he repented and wrote a refutation of his own earlier work. The majority of Shafi'i scholars followed al-Ash'ari's final position, though some criticized him on specific points like the identity of 'takwin' (creative power) and 'mukawwan' (the created). The author permits studying al-Ash'ari's books provided one is aware of his errors, and notes that many Ahl al-Sunnah scholars did so.

Key Terms
الحسن الأشعري
المعتزلة
الموجز الكبير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari was always a Sunni and never associated with Mu'tazila.
Correction: He was originally a Mu'tazili and authored works supporting them before Allah guided him to the truth.

Checkpoint
What did al-Ash'ari do after realizing the misguidance of the Mu'tazila?
A) He wrote a book defending them.
B) He wrote a refutation of what he had previously written for them.
C) He stopped writing altogether.
D) He became a philosopher.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's conversion from Mu'tazilism to Sunni orthodoxy is marked by his repentance and a refutation of his own earlier work, solidifying his role as a defender of Ahl al-Sunnah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you willing to publicly correct a previous error in your beliefs, even if it means humbling yourself before others? What would it take for you to disavow a mistaken conviction you once held with certainty?
?
How many of your actions or beliefs are you so attached to that you would refuse to change them even if Allah showed you their error? What is the one thing you know is wrong but haven't repented from?
?
Al-Ash'ari wrote a refutation of his own book. Can you point to a time when you actively worked to undo the harmful effects of your past mistakes on others? If not, what is stopping you from doing so today?

Shafi'i Acceptance and Caution on al-Ash'ari's Errors
Shafi'i acceptance and cautionary note

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that while most Shafi'i scholars adopted al-Ash'ari's final positions, some critiqued specific points like 'takwin' and 'mukawwan', and that studying his works is permissible with awareness of his errors.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's views were widely accepted by Shafi'is, but his errors require caution.

The second part of the passage explains the stance of Shafi'i scholars toward al-Ash'ari. Most followed his mature doctrine, but a few criticized him on certain matters, most notably his equation of 'takwin' and 'mukawwan'. The author permits studying his books provided one recognizes his mistakes, a practice that many Ahl al-Sunnah scholars followed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Shafi'i acceptance
Read the Arabic from 'وقد أخد عامة أصحاب الشافعي' to the end. Note the two groups: the majority who accepted his final views, and a minority who criticized him.
2
Identify the specific error mentioned
Find the example of an error: 'التكوين والمكون واحد'. Understand that this is a theological point about the attributes of Allah.
The author promises further explanation later.
3
Understand the permissibility of using his books
Notice the condition: 'فلا بأس له بالنظر في كتبه' provided one knows his errors. Many scholars kept and studied his works.

Al-Ash'ari's Diligence in Worship and Asceticism
A chain of transmission reports al-Ash'ari's twenty-year practice of praying Fajr with Isha wudu.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari's practice of praying Fajr with the wudu of Isha for twenty years exemplifies his diligence in worship and his humility in concealing his devotion.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's twenty-year practice shows constant worship and hidden piety.

This passage provides a firsthand account of al-Ash'ari's personal piety. Through a reliable chain of transmission, we learn of his remarkable devotional discipline and his humility in not publicizing his efforts. This lesson explores the significance of this practice.

Guided Path
1
Trace the Chain of Transmission
The passage begins with a full isnad, typical for transmitting authoritative accounts. Note the narrators and their reliability.
This adds credibility to the report.
2
Understand the Practice Described
Al-Ash'ari would pray Fajr with the wudu from Isha, meaning he remained in a state of ritual purity all night.
This indicates he spent the night in worship.
3
Reflect on Humility
The report also says he did not mention his devotion to anyone, showing his humility and sincerity.
True worship is done for Allah alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ذكر ماعرف من أبي الحسن رضى الله عنه من الاجتهاد في العبادة ونقل عنه من التقلل من الدنيا والزهادة
أخبرنا الشيخ أبو المظفر بن أبي العباس الشعيري الصوفي، قال أخبرنا الإمام أبو الفضل محمد بن على بن أحمد بن الحسين البسطامي، جدى لامی قال : سمعت علی بن محمد الطبرى المتكلم قال سمعت ابا الحسين السروى الفاضل في الكلام يقول : كان الشيخ أبو الحسن يعني الأشعري قريبا من عشرين سنة يصلى صلاة الصبح بوضوء العتمة، وكان لا يحكى عن اجتهاده شيئا إلى أحد .
Chapter: Mention of what is known of Abu al-Hasan (may Allah be pleased with him) regarding diligence in worship and what is transmitted from him of abstinence from the world and asceticism. The Shaykh Abu al-Muzaffar ibn Abi al-Abbas al-Sha'iri al-Sufi informed us, saying: The Imam Abu al-Fadl Muhammad ibn 'Ali ibn Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Bistami, my grandfather on my mother's side, said: I heard 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Tabari the mutakallim say: I heard Abu al-Husayn al-Sarawi, the excellent in speech, say: The Shaykh Abu al-Hasan—meaning al-Ash'ari—would pray the morning prayer with the wudu of the night prayer for nearly twenty years, and he would not mention anything of his devotion to anyone.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage introduces a new chapter on al-Ash'ari's personal piety. It provides a full chain of transmission (isnad) tracing back to a contemporary who observed al-Ash'ari. The key report is that al-Ash'ari regularly performed the Fajr (dawn) prayer using the same wudu (ablution) he had made for the 'Isha (night) prayer, indicating that he remained in a state of worship throughout the night. Moreover, he concealed his devotional efforts, not speaking of them to anyone, demonstrating humility.

Key Terms
الاجتهاد في العبادة
الزهادة
الوضوء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari's practice was merely a physical act without spiritual significance.
Correction: This practice is not merely a physical act but a sign of his deep spiritual state and constant worship.

Checkpoint
How long did al-Ash'ari maintain the practice of praying Fajr with the wudu of Isha?
A) 10 years.
B) 20 years.
C) 30 years.
D) 40 years.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's twenty-year practice of praying Fajr with Isha wudu illustrates his extraordinary devotion and humility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Ash'ari maintained his wudu from Isha to Fajr for twenty years—meaning his entire night was spent in a state of worship. When was the last time you remained in a state of wudu for even a few hours after prayer, mindful of Allah? What would it take for you to turn tonight from a night of sleep into a night of worship?
?
He concealed his devotion; no one knew the extent of his worship. What act of devotion have you done solely for Allah, hidden from every human eye? If none, what is holding you back from starting today?
?
Imagine standing before Allah on the Day of Judgment, and He asks you about your nights. Would your response include prolonged worship or mostly sleep and distraction? What one change can you make in your nightly routine starting tonight to draw closer to Allah?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
4 min
Al-Ash'ari's Repentance and the Shafi'i Reception
Ibn Asakir narrates al-Ash'ari's repentance and Shafi'i reception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ash'ari's transition from Mu'tazilism to Sunni orthodoxy and how the Shafi'i school received his teachings, including the specific issue of takwin and mukawwin.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari left Mu'tazilism after divine guidance; Shafi'is largely embraced his school.

Ibn Asakir begins by narrating that Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari was originally a Mu'tazili, but Allah showed him the error of their ways, leading him to repent and author a refutation of the Mu'tazila. He then explains that most Shafi'is adopted al-Ash'ari's final position, although some differed with him on certain issues—like the identity of takwin and mukawwin—and that such differences do not preclude benefiting from his works.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then the translation. Notice the sequence: al-Ash'ari's origin, his repentance, the Shafi'i adoption, and the mention of disagreement.
The passage covers al-Ash'ari's life and the reception of his school.
2
Identify al-Ash'ari's transformation
Note that al-Ash'ari started as a Mu'tazili, then Allah showed him the truth, so he repented and wrote a refutation. This is key to understanding his role as a Sunni theologian.
3
Understand the Shafi'i stance
Observe that most Shafi'is followed al-Ash'ari's final madhhab, but some scholars from Ahl al-Sunnah criticized him on specific issues like 'takwin and mukawwin are one'.
This shows the nuance in scholarly reception.
4
Reflect on the attitude towards his books
Even though some considered al-Ash'ari mistaken, many scholars still used his books after recognizing his errors. This sets the stage for the next lesson on proper attitude.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المعتزلة فى الابتداء، ثم ان الله تعالى بين له ضلالهم فبان عما اعتقده من مذهبهم وصنف كتابا ناقضا لما صنف للمعتزلة، وقد أخد عامة أصحاب الشافعي بما استقر عليه مذهب أبي الحسن الأشعرى وصنف أصحاب الشافعي كتبا كثيرة على وفق ما ذهب إليه الأشعرى إلا أن بعض أصحابنا من أهل السنة والجماعة خطأ أبا الحسن الأشعرى في بعض المسائل مثل قوله التكوين والمكون واحد ونحوها على ما يبين فى خلال المسائل ان شاء الله تعالى فمن وقف على المسائل التي أخطأ فيها أبو الحسن وعرف خطأه فلا بأس له بالنظر في كتبه فقد امسك كتبه كثير من أصحابنا من أهل السنة والجماعة ونظروا فيها . قال الامام الحافظ رضى الله عنه وهذه المسائل التي أشار إليها لا تكسب أبا الحسن تشنيعا ولا توجب له تكفيرا ولا تضليلا ولا تبديعا، ولو حققوا الكلام فيها لحصل الاتفاق وبان بأن الخلاف فيها حاصله الوفاق، ومازال العلماء يخالف بعضهم بعضا ويقصد دفع قول خصمه إبراما ونقضا ويجتهد في إظهاره خلافه بحثا وفحصا، ولا يعتقد ذلك في حقه عيبا ونقصا وقديما ما خالف ابا حنيفة صاحباه وأجابا في كثير من المسائل بما اباه والله يتغمد جميع العلماء برحمته ويحشرنا في زمرتهم بلطفه .ورأفته
The Mu'tazila in the beginning, then Allah Almighty showed him their error, so he repented from what he believed of their madhhab and authored a book refuting what the Mu'tazila authored. And the majority of the followers of al-Shafi'i adopted what the madhhab of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari settled upon, and the followers of al-Shafi'i authored many books in accordance with what al-Ash'ari went to, except that some of our companions from Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah considered Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari mistaken in some issues, such as his statement that al-takwin (originating) and al-mukawwin (the originator) are one, and similar matters, as will be explained in the issues, Allah willing. So whoever comes across the issues in which Abu al-Hasan erred and recognizes his error, there is no harm for him in looking at his books, for many of our companions from Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah have held onto his books and looked into them. The imam al-hafiz, may Allah be pleased with him, said: These issues which he pointed out do not earn Abu al-Hasan any disgrace, nor do they necessitate his takfir (declaring disbelief), nor his tadlil (declaring misguidance), nor his tabdi' (declaring innovation). And if they had investigated the speech concerning them, agreement would have been reached and it would become clear that the difference in them is essentially agreement. And scholars have always differed with one another, intending to rebut and refute the statement of their opponent, and they strive to show him to be in error through investigation and examination, and that is not considered in his regard a flaw or deficiency. And long ago, Abu Hanifa's two companions disagreed with him and answered in many issues with what he disapproved. And may Allah envelop all scholars with His mercy and gather us in their company with His grace and kindness.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is a historical and theological defense of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari by Ibn Asakir. It begins by stating that al-Ash'ari was originally a Mu'tazili, but Allah showed him the error of their ways, so he left them and wrote a refutation. Then it notes that most Shafi'is follow al-Ash'ari's madhhab, but some Ahl al-Sunnah disagreed with him on certain issues, like the identity of takwin and mukawwin. Ibn Asakir then argues that these disagreements do not warrant accusations of kufr, dhalal, or bid'a. He emphasizes that scholarly disagreement is normal and not a defect, citing the example of Abu Hanifa and his students. The passage serves to protect al-Ash'ari's reputation while acknowledging his mistakes.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
التكوين والمكون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What specific issue is mentioned as a point of disagreement with al-Ash'ari?
A) The attributes of Allah
B) The creation of the Quran
C) The identity of takwin and mukawwin
D) The status of sins

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's repentance from Mu'tazilism led to the formation of the Ash'ari school, which most Shafi'is adopted, despite some specific criticisms.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held a belief so strongly that you resisted changing it even when the truth became clear? What would it take for you to abandon a comfortable error, as al-Ash'ari did when he left the Mu'tazila after divine guidance? Will you sincerely ask Allah to show you your own blind spots today?
?
Al-Ash'ari's books were still studied by Sunni scholars despite his admitted mistakes. Do you have the humility to learn from flawed teachers, or do you reject everything from someone once you find an error? Think of a scholar or author you dismissed entirely after one disagreement—will you revisit their work with discernment?
?
The majority of Shafi'is adopted al-Ash'ari's school. Are you following a scholar or a group merely because it is popular or inherited from your family, without critically examining the evidence? Will you take time to verify the foundations of what you believe, even if it means questioning those you respect?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
4 min
Proper Attitude Towards a Scholar's Mistakes
Ibn Asakir defends al-Ash'ari and discusses the norm of scholarly disagreement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ibn Asakir argues that a scholar's mistakes do not warrant accusations of disbelief (takfir), misguidance (tadlil), or innovation (tabdi')—and how scholarly disagreement is a normal part of Islamic tradition.

Core Idea
Scholarly mistakes do not justify harsh judgments; disagreement is normal among scholars.

After mentioning that some scholars took issue with al-Ash'ari's positions, Ibn Asakir directly addresses the proper response. He asserts that these differences do not constitute disgrace, disbelief, misguidance, or innovation. He further explains that if the issues were properly investigated, they would actually lead to agreement, and he illustrates this by citing the historical example of Abu Hanifa and his two companions, who disagreed with him on many matters yet remained respected.

Guided Path
1
Read Ibn Asakir's main defense
Pay close attention to the phrase 'لا تكسب أبا الحسن تشنيعا ولا توجب له تكفيرا ولا تضليلا ولا تبديعا' – this is the core claim.
He lists four things that are not warranted: disgrace, takfir, tadlil, tabdi'.
2
Analyze the reasoning
Ibn Asakir argues that if one investigates the issues thoroughly, it becomes clear that the apparent disagreement is actually agreement ('الخلاف فيها حاصله الوفاق').
This suggests that deeper study resolves the tension.
3
Learn from the historical precedent
He cites the example of Abu Hanifa and his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, who disagreed with him on many issues. This shows that respectful disagreement has always been part of Islamic scholarship.
The example reinforces that disagreement is not a flaw.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Ibn Asakir ends with a prayer for mercy upon all scholars, emphasizing unity and respect across scholarly differences.
This frames the entire discussion in a spirit of inclusiveness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Mu'tazila in the beginning, then Allah Almighty showed him their error, so he repented from what he believed of their madhhab and authored a book refuting what the Mu'tazila authored. And the majority of the followers of al-Shafi'i adopted what the madhhab of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari settled upon, and the followers of al-Shafi'i authored many books in accordance with what al-Ash'ari went to, except that some of our companions from Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah considered Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari mistaken in some issues, such as his statement that al-takwin (originating) and al-mukawwin (the originator) are one, and similar matters, as will be explained in the issues, Allah willing. So whoever comes across the issues in which Abu al-Hasan erred and recognizes his error, there is no harm for him in looking at his books, for many of our companions from Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah have held onto his books and looked into them. The imam al-hafiz, may Allah be pleased with him, said: These issues which he pointed out do not earn Abu al-Hasan any disgrace, nor do they necessitate his takfir (declaring disbelief), nor his tadlil (declaring misguidance), nor his tabdi' (declaring innovation). And if they had investigated the speech concerning them, agreement would have been reached and it would become clear that the difference in them is essentially agreement. And scholars have always differed with one another, intending to rebut and refute the statement of their opponent, and they strive to show him to be in error through investigation and examination, and that is not considered in his regard a flaw or deficiency. And long ago, Abu Hanifa's two companions disagreed with him and answered in many issues with what he disapproved. And may Allah envelop all scholars with His mercy and gather us in their company with His grace and kindness.

Commentary
This passage is a historical and theological defense of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari by Ibn Asakir. It begins by stating that al-Ash'ari was originally a Mu'tazili, but Allah showed him the error of their ways, so he left them and wrote a refutation. Then it notes that most Shafi'is follow al-Ash'ari's madhhab, but some Ahl al-Sunnah disagreed with him on certain issues, like the identity of takwin and mukawwin. Ibn Asakir then argues that these disagreements do not warrant accusations of kufr, dhalal, or bid'a. He emphasizes that scholarly disagreement is normal and not a defect, citing the example of Abu Hanifa and his students. The passage serves to protect al-Ash'ari's reputation while acknowledging his mistakes.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Asakir, what do the issues in which al-Ash'ari was mistaken not necessitate?
A) Any scholarly discussion

Key Takeaway
Scholarly mistakes do not warrant harsh accusations; respectful disagreement has always been part of Islamic scholarship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear of a scholar's mistake, what is your first inner reaction? Do you find yourself thinking less of them? What would it take for you to respond as Ibn Asakir teaches—without disgrace, takfir, tadlil, or tabdi'?
?
Think of a scholar you respect who may have made an error in 'aqeedah. Does this lesson allow you to continue learning from them? Or do you hold a hidden judgment that needs to be released? What would it mean for your heart to truly embrace that their mistake does not warrant condemnation?
?
If you were in a position of teaching or authority, how would you handle a student's theological mistake after internalizing this passage? Are you more lenient with yourself than with others? What specific step can you take this week to apply the principle of respectful disagreement in a real relationship?
